Note: "Fan" is a Japanese unit, approximately equal to 1.25 Chinese Mu.

From the above two tables, the occupational status and agricultural situation of Koreans in our Northeast can be seen at a glance. According to the Korean Residents Association, among the more than 7,000 Koreans under its jurisdiction, the majority are agricultural laborers. Others engaged in innkeeping, prostitution, and serving as maids number over 300, while those without any occupation exceed 100. The above table is copied from the Liaoning Korean Residents Association. Their classification of occupations differs from our concept of occupation. What they call "maids" is actually a euphemism for prostitutes, and there is no real difference between them and the prostitutes in brothels. Furthermore, the "other freelancers" and "other employed" listed in the table should be regarded as having no legitimate occupation. Even among those in "commerce and consignment," "medicine," and "employees of various companies," a significant portion may be unemployed idlers, engaged in selling contraband, and other improper businesses. Although this table is a statistical summary of the occupations of Koreans in a part of Liaoning, the occupational distribution of Koreans in other regions is generally the same. As for their agricultural situation, it is truly alarming to us. The paddy and dry rice fields cultivated by them in the three northeastern provinces reach 2,831,870 Fan, equivalent to more than 3,539,830 Chinese Mu. The land that can be used for paddy field cultivation in the future is still 3,416,021 Fan, equivalent to more than 4,270,000 Chinese Mu. The current annual harvest of brown rice is over 940,000 Shi. If further developed in the future, it will surely double. This large amount of food, in addition to being consumed by the local Koreans themselves each year, is mostly shipped to Japan. At a time when our country is facing a shortage of food and the number of starving people is increasing daily, allowing such vast farmlands to be developed and seized by foreigners is a strategic mistake that could not be worse. (To be continued)

Important News

Agreement on the Recovery of the Shanghai French Concession Mixed Court

▲ Chinese Court to be Established in the French Concession

▲ Signed in Beijing on the 28th

The agreement on the recovery of the Shanghai French Concession Mixed Court was officially signed in Beijing on the 28th of this month. The full text of the agreement consists of 14 articles and one annex. It was officially announced by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs this morning (29th). The full text is as follows:

▲ Agreement on the Establishment of a Chinese Court in the Shanghai French Concession (Article 1) From the date of entry into force of this Agreement, the agency currently established in the Shanghai French Concession, namely the Mixed Court, and all related regulations and practices, shall be abolished. (Article 2) The Chinese government, in accordance with Chinese laws and regulations regarding judicial administration, shall establish a District Court and a Branch of the High Court in the Shanghai French Concession. Each court shall have dedicated personnel and shall exercise its jurisdiction only within the boundaries of the Concession. Appeals against the judgments and rulings of the Branch of the High Court shall be accepted by the Chinese Supreme Court in accordance with Chinese law. (Article 3) The current effective and future legally enacted and promulgated laws and regulations of China shall apply equally to each court, taking into account the administrative regulations of the Concession. (Article 4) Each court shall establish a Procuratorate, whose personnel shall be appointed by the Chinese government. These prosecutors shall handle inspection matters and perform their duties in accordance with Chinese law with respect to all cases involving Articles 103 to 186 of the Criminal Code, except in cases where the Concession authorities or the injured party have filed a lawsuit. The prosecutor's investigation procedures shall be public, and the defendant may be assisted by a lawyer. Other cases occurring within the jurisdiction of each court shall be prosecuted by the Concession authorities or initiated by the injured party. The prosecutor shall have the right to appear in court and express opinions on all criminal cases brought by the Concession authorities or the injured party. (Article 5) All litigation documents and judgments shall be effective after being signed by a judge of the above-mentioned court. Once signed, they shall be served or executed separately. (Article 6) Any person arrested in the Concession shall be handed over to the competent court within 24 hours, excluding holidays. Failure to do so shall result in immediate release. (Article 7) No suspect shall be transferred to an office outside the Concession without prior interrogation by the competent court. The defendant may be assisted by a lawyer. However, if the transfer is entrusted by another Chinese modern court and the court confirms that it is the person in question, the transfer shall be carried out immediately. (Article 8) The Concession authorities, upon request for assistance, shall do their utmost to provide such assistance within their authority so that the judgments of the two courts can be executed. (Article 9) The presidents of each court shall appoint clerks to perform their duties in the civil divisions of each court. The clerks shall deliver summons and other litigation documents, but when executing judgments, they shall be accompanied by judicial police. The judicial police shall provide assistance when requested. (Article 10) Judicial police officers, including police officers, shall be appointed by the president of the Branch of the High Court upon recommendation by the Concession authorities. The president of the Branch of the High Court may terminate the duties of the judicial police on his own initiative or at the request of the Concession authorities, stating the reasons. The judicial police shall wear Chinese uniforms, be subject to the orders and directions of each court, and be loyal to their duties. (Article 11) The detention facilities attached to the public offices referred to in Article 1 of this Agreement shall hereafter be entirely under the management of the Chinese judicial authorities. Each court, within its jurisdiction, may decide to have prisoners serving sentences in the above-mentioned detention facilities continue to serve their sentences in those facilities, or transfer them to prisons outside the Concession. Each court may also designate the place of imprisonment for prisoners sentenced by the court. However, those punished for violating Chinese police regulations or Concession administrative regulations shall not be detained in detention facilities in the Concession. All prisoners sentenced to death shall be sent to the neighboring Chinese authorities. (Article 12) Lawyers of French or other foreign nationality may appear in the two courts, but must hold a lawyer's certificate issued by the Chinese Ministry of Judicial Administration in accordance with Chinese laws and regulations, and must comply with Chinese laws and regulations regarding the duties of lawyers, including disciplinary regulations. The above-mentioned lawyers of French or other non-Chinese nationality shall handle cases in which non-Chinese nationals are parties, and only represent such parties. When the Concession authorities are the plaintiff, complainant, or participant, or have filed criminal proceedings, they may employ not only Chinese lawyers but also lawyers of French or other nationality. The Concession authorities may, in cases deemed to be in the interests of the Concession, submit opinions in writing solely by lawyers, or participate in litigation in accordance with the Chinese Code of Civil Procedure. (Article 13) The Chinese and French governments shall each appoint two permanent representatives. If differences of opinion arise regarding the interpretation or application of this Agreement, the president of the Branch of the High Court or the French Minister to China may refer the differences of opinion to the representatives for joint discussion. However, the opinions of the representatives shall not be binding on the Chinese or French governments unless agreed to by both governments. Furthermore, the orders, judgments, or rulings of each court shall not be subject to discussion by the representatives. (Article 14) This Agreement and the attached exchange of notes shall be effective from July 31, 1931, to April 1, 1933. With the consent of the Chinese and French governments, it may be extended for three years. This Agreement is signed in Nanjing in two copies each in Chinese and French. The Chinese and French texts have been carefully proofread and are without error. July 28, 1931, the 20th year of the Republic of China. Xu Mo, Wu Kunwu (representing the Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China). Leger, Gangeland (representing the French Minister to China).

▲ Annex (1) Mr. Wei, Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the French Republic to China, communicates this note. Having today signed with Your Excellency the Minister the Agreement on the Establishment of a Chinese Court in the Shanghai French Concession, I request Your Excellency the Minister to provide proof of agreement with the following points: (1) All houses and movable property belonging to the public offices referred to in Article 1 of this Agreement, together with documents and bank deposits, shall be transferred to the two courts. (2) The president of the Branch of the High Court shall allocate an office within the premises of the court to one of the judicial police officers designated by the Concession authorities, so that he may record all judicial documents such as summons, arrest warrants, rulings, and judgments. (3) The Concession authorities shall, to the extent practicable, select Chinese people to serve as judicial police officers. (4) The Chinese government, upon the recommendation of the French government, shall appoint an advisor without pay. The advisor may submit suggestions and opinions to the Chinese judicial authorities regarding the Concession prison system and its administration. (5) All judgments made by the public offices referred to in Article 1 of this Agreement shall have the effect of final judgment, except for those that have been appealed or are still subject to appeal. (6) All cases under the jurisdiction of the two courts in accordance with the provisions of this Agreement that have not been concluded on the date of entry into force of this Agreement shall be transferred to each court immediately. Each court shall, to the extent possible, consider the previous litigation procedures to have been determined and endeavor to adjudicate the above-mentioned cases within twelve months, but this period may be extended if necessary. (7) All items confiscated or seized at the time of conviction in accordance with Chinese law shall be stored within the premises of the two courts and disposed of by the Chinese government. Opium and opium-related paraphernalia shall be publicly burned in the Concession every three months. As for the disposal of firearms, the Concession authorities may suggest methods, which shall be forwarded to the Chinese government through the presidents of each court. I respectfully request that you take note of this and reply accordingly. It is necessary to send this note. To His Excellency Wang, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China. July 28, 1931. Leger, Gangeland (representing the French Minister to China). (2) His Excellency Wang, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China, is responding to your letter regarding the Agreement on the Establishment of a Chinese Court in the Shanghai French Concession signed today. I, the Minister, hereby declare to Your Excellency the Minister that I agree with and confirm the points made in your letter: (1) All houses and movable property belonging to the public offices referred to in Article 1 of this Agreement, together with documents and bank deposits, shall be transferred to the two courts. (2) The president of the Branch of the High Court shall allocate an office within the premises of the court to one of the judicial police officers designated by the Concession authorities, so that he may record all judicial documents such as summons, arrest warrants, rulings, and judgments. (3) The Concession authorities shall, to the extent practicable, select Chinese people to serve as judicial police officers. (4) The Chinese government, upon the recommendation of the French government, shall appoint an advisor without pay. The advisor may submit suggestions and opinions to the Chinese judicial authorities regarding the Concession prison system and its administration. (5) All judgments made by the public offices referred to in Article 1 of this Agreement shall have the effect of final judgment, except for those that have been appealed or are still subject to appeal. (6) All cases under the jurisdiction of the two courts in accordance with the provisions of this Agreement that have not been concluded on the date of entry into force of this Agreement shall be transferred to each court immediately. Each court shall, to the extent possible, consider the previous litigation procedures to have been determined and endeavor to adjudicate the above-mentioned cases within twelve months, but this period may be extended if necessary. (7) All items confiscated or seized at the time of conviction in accordance with Chinese law shall be stored within the premises of the two courts and disposed of by the Chinese government. Opium and opium-related paraphernalia shall be publicly burned in the Concession every three months. As for the disposal of firearms, the Concession authorities may suggest methods, which shall be forwarded to the Chinese government through the presidents of each court. I respectfully respond to your request to take note of this. It is necessary to send this note. To His Excellency Wei, Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the French Republic to China. July 28, 1931, the 20th year of the Republic of China. Xu Mo, Wu Kunwu (representing the Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China).

Japanese Essentially Occupying Wanbaoshan

▲ Local Negotiations Completely Ineffective

▲ Japanese Troops Stationed in Wanbaoshan Continuously Reinforced

▲ Dammed Water Rising, Farmers Appeal

▲ Situation Deteriorating Further

Changchun Dispatch: Regarding the Wanbaoshan Incident, the central government has considered it a local issue and has not lodged a serious protest with the Japanese side. However, the Japanese side views the occupation of Wanbaoshan as part of their plan to occupy Manchuria and Mongolia. They are therefore pleased that our central government is not paying attention to the Wanbaoshan case and are actively developing their plan. Consequently, they are completely rejecting our side's demands regarding local negotiations. At the same time, they are also increasing troop deployments in the Mashaokou area. In other words, Wanbaoshan is no longer ours. Therefore, all sectors here greatly hope that the central government will lodge a serious protest with the Japanese side regarding the Wanbaoshan case, and not regard the case as entirely separate from the Korean massacre of overseas Chinese, treating it lightly and allowing the cunning schemes of the Japanese to succeed. The following is a record of the recent situation of this case:

▲ Unreasonable Demands from the Japanese Side According to a Japanese reporter in China, negotiations regarding the Wan Incident have stalled due to the stalemate between the two sides. The Chinese side insists that the issue cannot be resolved unless Korean farmers stop working, Japanese police withdraw, and rice paddy leases are terminated. The ultimate concession they are willing to make is limited to compensating the Korean farmers for their losses. The Japanese side demands that the contract between Hao Yongde and the Korean farmers be considered valid and denies the Chinese side's claim for compensation, which is a prerequisite. Ultimately, they insist on allowing Korean farmers to plant rice as agreed, with the ditch embankments occupying some civilian farmland, leasing land according to the contract, and achieving the completion of the farm plan before stopping. Mayor Zhou and the Japanese consul, in addition to formal official protests, have also repeatedly negotiated on this point of contention, with neither side willing to back down. The Chinese side believes that the issue of land sovereignty is of utmost importance, so they will not concede. The Japanese side insists on continuing to fight, not stopping until their goal is achieved, because a long-standing pre-determined plan is now being realized. Since the two sides are moving in opposite directions, a solution may not be easily reached in the short term. It is heard that Japanese officials, after discussions at the consulate, have decided to send Kuramoto to the municipal government to present eight demands orally, followed by a formal official letter. They also decided on a final solution: if the Chinese authorities are willing to compensate the Korean farmers for their losses, the total amount of the Korean farmers' losses will be calculated as compensation for ten years. The lease will also be stipulated to expire in ten years. All rice paddies will be calculated as 500 qing, with each qing yielding a certain amount of rice and wheat each year, and each stone priced at a certain amount of yuan. The compensation for ten years of losses will be calculated based on a very bountiful harvest each year, and the Chinese government will pay it during the autumn harvest. This is one aspect. Another part is the cost of digging trenches and building dams by Korean farmers in the Wanbaoshan Mashaokou rice area this year, as well as the cost of sending Japanese troops to protect them, all calculated in full, and the Chinese side must be responsible for compensating it. This is the second aspect. These two unreasonable demands are the Japanese side's final means of resistance. If Chinese officials can agree, it can also be resolved, they say. These demands are tantamount to seizing our rice paddies by force. Moreover, everyone who is close to the Japanese side says the same thing, which shows the determination of the Japanese to occupy Wanbaoshan Town.

▲ Japanese Side Withdraws Police and Reinforces Troops During the Wan Incident, Japanese troops occupied Mashaokou, and armed police officers were transferred one after another. Therefore, the defense of the Japanese concession was insufficient. According to those close to the Japanese, Consul Tashiro is secretly withdrawing some of the Japanese police who were previously dispatched for this reason. However, there are still thirty to forty Japanese police officers left to protect the rice paddies. Fearing that their force is weak, they have specially dispatched two teams of fifteen garrison soldiers each to assist in reinforcement. In addition, there are Japanese plainclothes teams and Korean self-defense militia groups stationed in Mashaokou, totaling no less than one hundred and several dozen troops. The Japanese side also declared that they would dispatch large numbers of troops if necessary. Otherwise, the rumor that the Japanese police team would not be dispatched and that the Japanese Consul-General in Liaoning, Hayashi Hisashi, telegraphed Tashiro to withdraw all police teams stationed in Ma, has not been realized to this day. The secret withdrawals and retreats at night in recent days are purely a contingency plan automatically deployed by the Japanese consul, and not the result of our side's demand for police withdrawal. The garrison team assisting in the defense of Ma departed on the nights of the 19th and 20th. On the surface, it seems to be a partial withdrawal of troops and police, but in reality, it is a substitution, a change of soup but not of medicine.

▲ Flood After the Dam is Built After the Koreans completed the construction of the dam in Mashaokou, the water level rose sharply. The Korean farmers then released water to irrigate their fields. Since the 13th, nearby civilian fields have been flooded, about 250 to 260 hectares. From the 18th to the 19th and 20th, there were continuous heavy rains and hailstorms in the Jilin-Changchun area. The Yitong River flooded, and torrents of mountain water surged down, overflowing both banks. According to representatives of Chinese farmers from Guanhuang Guantun, Sanxingtun, Jiangjiawobao, Huajiaqiao, and Liangyimen downstream—Jiang Hongshan, Liu Changjiang, Ma Zhenqing, Tian Jun, and Gong De—who came to Changchun on the 20th to report to the county government and the municipal government, the Yitong River water level gradually rose after the Korean farmers built the dam, with the deepest part a few inches from the bank. In recent days, rain and hail have alternated, and the river water has overflowed, breaking the dam in the middle of the stream, causing flooding on both banks. The area of civilian fields flooded upstream and downstream has now reached 1,500 to 1,600 hectares. If there is another heavy rain, the crops on the sloping 5,000 to 6,000 hectares of land will inevitably be destroyed. If the dam is removed, the water level will drop immediately. If proper prevention and removal of the dam are not carried out, the civilian fields along the river will become a swamp, and the lives and property of hundreds of thousands of farmers will be washed away. The autumn harvest is already half hopeless, they said. Mayor Zhou and County Magistrate Ma, after receiving the report, have decided to lodge a protest, demanding that the Japanese consul quickly order the Korean farmers to remove the dam.

▲ Japanese Rescue Koreans Due to the lack of food, the Korean farmers in Mashaokou are quite panic-stricken. Korean laborers are given a full meal of rice per day, and the rest eat porridge in the morning and evening. Consul Tashiro therefore specially ordered Tokusuke Shimotoku, the chairman of the Wan Incident Support Association for Japanese citizens in Tougou, to convene a committee meeting to discuss relief measures. The meeting was held on the 19th. The chairman of the Veterans Association, Shiido; the chairman of the local committee, Kazuki; the chairman of the Residents Association, Tanaka; the chairman of the Autonomous League, Hakoda; the chairman of the Youth Federation, Ozawa; and the police chief, Takenami; and the chief of the consulate, Kuramoto, all attended. They decided to raise funds for relief and purchase and transport food. Shimotoku, Shiido, Tanaka, Hakoda, and Takenami are responsible for handling the matter. The fundraising methods are: (1) Japanese and Korean merchants and citizens, regardless of gender, age, or youth, donate a voluntary donation of 20 sen of Japanese yen per person per month, which is paid monthly. Shimotoku, Shiido, and others, in conjunction with the Japanese police, solicit donations from house to house. (2) Free donations should be submitted to the North Manchuria Daily, the Business News, and the Asahi Shimbun branch, and transferred to the Support Association to purchase food and transport it to Mashaokou, where it is distributed by the director of the Inada Japanese Police Station, Nakagawa. It is currently heard that they are temporarily raising 3,000 yen of Japanese money for relief. If it is not enough, they will continue to raise funds. (22nd)

An Observation Journal of Pyongyang

▲ The Current State of Overseas Chinese in Pyongyang Your reporter departed from Andong at 9:30 PM on July 22nd and arrived in Pyongyang at 3:30 AM on the 23rd. Upon disembarking from the train, a criminal detective from the Government-General of Korea was there to protect him, claiming that he was there to protect him under orders from his superiors. When asked how he knew the reporter was coming, he smiled and did not answer, only taking his leave after the reporter had checked into the Sanken-shi Inn. At 8:00 AM, the reporter was still asleep when he was suddenly awakened by someone calling out, identifying himself as Han Pei-chang.

The State of Torn Silk and Cloth After the Robbery of Qian Hesheng Silk Shop in Pyongyang

A Shandong native, manager of the Taikwan Foreign Firm in Pyongyang, because he heard people at the Inn talking, and that three Chinese have checked into this inn, hence the visit to inquire, after revealing my place of origin, he detailed the horrific events that happened in Pyongyang, that the Taian Foreign Firm was established by an American, and he has been the manager for 24 years, his whole family resided here, had a 76 year old mother, with his wife and 7 children. Now the firm has been completely destroyed by Koreans, his personal savings of decades has been completely destroyed, a daughter aged 14, due to shock and fright, died in hospital. Thankfully, his elderly mother is still healthy and sound. He teared up as he spoke, choking with emotions. The reporter felt a great sorrow, his eyes welling with tears. Around 10:00 AM, the head of the Pyongyang Chinese Business Association, Meng Xianshi, the permanent committee members, Liu Ziping and Wang Zichen, came after hearing the news to visit. They discussed in great detail the causes and the details of the damages suffered, they said that there were originally seven thousand Chinese overseas, most have since fled back to their country after the incident, currently residing in Pyongyang City are about two hundred odd people, residing in the countryside, about two hundred odd people, in hospital there are fifty odd people, calculating men and women, there were fewer than 600 people. From July 6th onwards, the Japanese police had sent them to live in temporary shelters, until the 18th, did they begin to leave the shelters one after another. The Japanese official shelters, until the 20th it closed down. The leaving overseas Chinese, by the Japanese police were instructed to live in 5 places, in the city, there were 4 places, (1) residing in Qian Hesheng, there were 60 people, of which, there were 2 women, the men were all businessmen (2) residing in Dong Shenglou, there were 28 people, all were counter staff from restaurants (3) residing in Hong Shenglou, there were 85 people, of which there were 4 women, the men were all shops

The Messy State of Robbed Shops in Pyongyang

Counter staff and vegetable garden workers (4) residing at Yong Sheng Gong, there were 137 people, of which there were 24 women, the men were all laborers. The above mentioned 4 places, the Japanese official called them temporary shelters, with one

Page 10

Two, Three and Four designation, aside from that, there were vegetable garden workers, about two hundred odd people, working in the countryside, and every night resided in one location, by the Japanese police for protection, all the overseas Chinese, daily resided at the shelters, daring not to go out, those that had matters and had to go out, dared not to go far, some disguised themselves as Japanese Koreans, and that might be able to avoid it, otherwise, walking on lonely and secluded places, still could not avoid being sniped at by Koreans. Minister Wang Rongbao, recently arrived in Pyongyang, and negotiated with the Japanese authorities, and requested protection from the Japanese authorities, and asked all overseas Chinese, to visit the various debtor residences, and audit and reconcile the debts, and retrieve the debts. However, the Koreans already knew that the overseas Chinese books have been destroyed, and cunningly refused to pay, as for the various shops, all were destroyed beyond recognition, difficult to recover, aside from Hong Shenglou restaurant, as the damage was more slight, and has voluntarily sought to resume business, all the other 300 odd large and small shops, had no hope of resuming business.

▲ A Visit to the Hospital At 11:30, Fujida Katsusaburo, the industry head of Pyongyang City Hall, and patrolman Mori Ogahiro, arrived at the hotel, claiming to be there to protect us under orders, and asked permission to follow us everywhere. Although we knew they were monitoring us, we had no way to refuse, so we went with them to the Pingnam Provincial Hall and Pyongyang City Hall to pay our respects to Governor Sonoda Hiroshi and Oshima Yoshi, and at 12:00 we went to the Pyongyang Shih Hospital to visit the overseas Chinese compatriots who were recovering in the hospital. The hospital had accommodated 110 injured overseas Chinese after the incident, including 8 women. 18 people died after being admitted to the hospital, including 4 women. After treatment, 50 odd people were discharged from the hospital, and there are currently 41 men and 4 women in the hospital. This was all said by the hospital director. When asked to see the list of casualties, he claimed that it had been sent to the provincial hall and was not kept in the hospital. The overseas Chinese were living in the lowest-grade third-class rooms in the hospital. The mats were broken and the rooms were dirty. Each room accommodated seven or eight people, and the air was extremely turbid. Each person was wrapped in dirty and old bandages. This proves that the hospital is not doing its best to treat the wounded. The wounds of each injured person were all on the head, wrists, arms, legs, etc. One overseas Chinese compatriot had wounds all over his body, and his left eye was covered by a bandage. He was lying on the ground moaning incessantly. A fellow injured person in the same room said that his left eye was broken and he was already blind. He had been injured for many days and had not yet recovered. The other injured people were also lying on the ground crying in pain. It was unbearable to hear their voices and unbearable to see their condition. The reporter intended to take a photo, but as soon as the light was adjusted, the Japanese hospital director sternly stopped him, saying that photography was not allowed here. Therefore, such a tragic scene could not be captured in a photo to report to the people of the country. Among the women recovering, there was one, Madam Zhu Li, who cried when she saw the reporter, recounting that her husband had been beaten to death, and an eight-year-old son had also been killed. Only she and her three-year-old son remained in her arms. The reporter listened to her account and wanted to find a word of comfort, but he didn't know what to do. Since entering the hospital, the overseas Chinese had not seen a single relative or friend for nearly a month. Knowing that the reporter was Chinese, they were all moved to tears and wanted to pour out their grievances, but the hospital director repeatedly stopped them from talking, and urged them to leave quickly on the grounds that other Japanese and Korean patients in the hospital hated the noise. Reluctantly, they left the hospital with tears in their eyes. Walking in the courtyard, they still saw the injured overseas Chinese compatriots watching from the windows, each with tears in their eyes, looking longingly. At that moment, the reporter's brain was filled with hot blood, and his head was dizzy. He didn't know whether he felt sour or bitter.

▲ Graves of Overseas Chinese Compatriots Who Died Tragically After leaving the Pyongyang Hospital, we went to the fake tombs of the overseas Chinese compatriots who died tragically outside the city. The place is at the foot of Changshan Mountain in the Datong Hall, more than ten miles from Pyongyang City. Driving, we saw five burnt vegetable gardens and houses by the roadside. Broken bricks and tiles were everywhere. In particular, a vermicelli workshop was burned the most tragically. Only a dozen broken beams and broken pillars, and two unburned brick chimneys remained on the ground. Generally, Korean women, old and young,

Condition After Destruction of Vegetable Gardens in the Countryside of Pyongyang

They were squatting in the vegetable gardens, searching for fruits and vegetables. These people have simple minds and do not know that they are being used. After an hour, we arrived at the fake tomb. The tombs of the 95 people who died, as they are called, are just five large ridges of earth, with an incense table and two wreaths from the mayor in front. There are four soil pits, three zhang long and one zhang and three chi wide, and one soil pit two zhang long, with the same width. According to Fujida, who guided us, each soil pit contains 20 people, and the smaller ones contain 15 people, for a total of 95 people. Before burial, the provincial hall compiled numbers and kept a clear list of faces for a year, so that the Chinese side could check later. A numbered stake was placed in front of the body to match the list of faces. However, according to the reporter's measurements, each pit contains at least 35 or 6 people, and the five pits together contain more than 160 or 70 people. We took a photo and waited to develop and map it when we returned. Later, we offered incense and paid our respects with our companions, and after a half-day of mourning, we returned to the city.

▲ Inspection of Destroyed Shops The shops of overseas Chinese were mostly destroyed in the Korean residential area, and the Japanese residential area was less damaged. In silk shops such as Qian Hesheng and Yong Qingde, doors and windows were broken, and goods that were of good quality and valuable were looted, while those of poor quality were torn into thin strips and trampled on. In the case of Qian Hexiang, about 100 bolts of linen and ramie cloth were torn. The rest of the halls, such as Donghua Yuan, were the most severely damaged. The furniture upstairs and downstairs was not intact, and even the doors, windows, and walls were torn to pieces. Among the destroyed shops, this number was the most serious. In the Yong Sheng Gong ironware factory, the boilers and other items stored were destroyed by hammers and axes. Fortunately, the factory cast its own products, and the raw materials were still available. With some work, they could still be made into objects. The walls and roofs of the Chinese Chamber of Commerce were all uncovered and broken.

Condition After Destruction of the Taiyuan Restaurant, a Chinese Restaurant in Pyongyang

For now, the broken house of Qian Hexiang is used as a temporary office, temporarily handling the investigation of the deaths of overseas Chinese. Because most of the staff are managers and shareholders of the destroyed shops, they are not in the mood to work after the disaster. Therefore, the Beijing Chinese Chamber of Commerce specially sent Zhou Zhaogao, Wang Gongwen, Zhang Youfang, Liu Shoufu, and Zhou Baoshan, and Zhao Zhongxuan and Wang Minghao from Incheon, to help with the aftermath. The reporter also visited each temporary shelter for a week. Each shelter was guarded by a Japanese policeman to prevent accidents. The displaced masses did not go out into the streets unless they had to. It can be said that there were no traces of overseas Chinese. The official Sonoda Hiroshi gave each deceased overseas Chinese compatriot a consolation fee of 500 yen (Japanese money), which was received by the family members of the deceased and certified by the Chinese Chamber of Commerce. The injured were given 50 yuan. So far, 29 people have received the consolation fee for tragic deaths, and about 50 odd people have received the injury fee.

▲ A Conversation with the Governor Pyongyang belongs to Pingnam Province. The governor of the province is equal to the Tao Yin in our country, but the powers of police, education, finance, and municipal administration all belong to him. The Japanese who accompanied him insisted on seeing Governor Sonoda Hiroshi and Oshima Yoshi, the mayor of Pyongyang (equivalent to the mayor of our country). The reporter asked about the handling of the aftermath of the overseas Chinese. Sonoda Hiroshi said that this incident was sudden and he regretted not being able to prevent it. There is no definite number of overseas Chinese in Pyongyang, about 6,000 people. At the time of the incident, they were protected by the police and sent to a temporary shelter, which housed more than 5,000 people. To prepare food and lodging, a large team of police was dispatched to protect them day and night. Those who returned to Shandong were sent to Zhennampo free of charge to take a sea ship. The provincial hall also sent a few yuan for pocket money. The shelter was closed on the 20th, and the remaining overseas Chinese were taken over by the Chamber of Commerce. The provincial hall gave them ten days of food. Those who had debts with the outside world, although the account books were damaged, have been instructed to check with each other to resolve the debts. The provincial hall will try to make it easy to resolve. Mayor Oshima Yoshi has less responsibility for the tragedy, so he only spoke with modesty. (Sent from Keijo on the 25th)

The Water Level of the Canal Continues to Rise, the Jiangsu Provincial Government Decides to Open the Cheluo Dam

▲ Earth will be opened twice when it reaches one zhang, seven chi, and three cun.

Zhenjiang Dispatch: The water level of the Jiangbei border river in Jiangsu Province has continued to rise in the past two days. According to reports from the Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau, the water level at Gaoyou Yumato rose two cun before noon on the 27th, with a water level of one zhang, six chi, and seven cun, and another cun in the afternoon, with a water level of one zhang, six chi, and eight cun. On the morning of the 28th, it continued to rise by two cun, and the water level reached one zhang, seven chi, which is almost the same as the size of the Guihai Dam that was opened in 1921. Sun Hongzhe, the director of the Construction Department, considered the situation serious and specially proposed to the provincial government to consider the public opinion and water level and approve the appropriate size for opening the dam. The provincial government decided yesterday that when the water level reaches one zhang, seven chi, and three cun, the Cheluo Dam will be opened in two stages. Half of it will be opened first, and if the water continues to rise, the other half will be opened. The Construction Department has telegraphed Director Mao and Section Chief Qian, who are stationed in Gaoyou, to inform them. The water level in Yaowan fell by six points and six centimeters yesterday, but the water level is still 17.93 meters. If Bengbu can also fall like this and does not continue to rise, the Guihai Dam may not need to be fully opened.

The Jiangsu Provincial Agricultural Department Relieves the Silkworm Famine

▲ Advocating Autumn Silkworm Breeding and Increasing the Number of Guidance Centers

Zhenjiang Dispatch: Jiangsu Province suffered from poor spring silkworm breeding this year due to the influence of the weather, and the rural economy suffered heavy losses. If we do not make every effort to promote autumn silkworm breeding, it will not be enough to make up for the losses. In view of this, the Agricultural Department, in addition to the 50 odd autumn silkworm guidance centers attached to the various county fields, has also joined the China United Sericulture Improvement Association this year to establish five guidance centers in important areas, such as Huangxu in Zhenjiang, Taowu in Jiangning, Xinzhou in Yangzhou, and Jurong Yizheng. The total autumn planting production in the province is no less than one million and several hundred thousand sheets, which is enough for distribution. It is also heard that the Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee, based on the submission of the Zhenjiang County Executive Committee, which was submitted by Sun Danzhen and Wang Jinshan, requesting to prepare a large amount of autumn seed and vigorously encourage breeding to alleviate the silkworm famine, sent a letter to the department for investigation. The department replied in the above situation and ordered the counties to follow the original plan. If the weather can clear up in the future, the results will be considerable.

Wuxi

Two Suicide Cases in One Day: A resident of this county, Xu Yangsen, aged 49, living near Xinglong Bridge in Lichengjiao, was the owner of Hongyishun Meat Shop in Badou Alley. His wife, Wu, had borne him seven children. In the autumn of last year, Yangsen suddenly suffered from a nervous disorder, behaving like a madman all day long. Although he sought medical treatment, it was to no avail. Yesterday (29th) at 11:00 AM, Yangsen took a yellow hemp rope in his room and hanged himself from the doorframe next to the stairs. His wife, Wu, discovered him and immediately cut the rope, but Yangsen had already died. It was indeed a tragic sight. Also, near Rihui Bridge outside the South Gate, in Huolong Alley, the cook Pang Bingsheng, aged 43, at the residence of Li, was from Masi Bridge in Changshu. The day before yesterday, for unknown reasons, Bingsheng hanged himself and died. Yesterday, the local Tutouzheng, Tan Bing'an, reported the case to the County Court, requesting that officials be dispatched to investigate.

Bandits Commit Robbery, Killing a Housewife: In Jingwei, Fifth District, Section 54, a local villager, Shi Fujin, recently received over 200 yuan in Shuishuiyang, which attracted the attention of bandits. On the night of the 28th, around 11:00 PM, seven bandits suddenly broke into his house and committed a major robbery. They also shot and killed Fu Jin's wife, Wan. The robbery lasted for about an hour before the bandits fled with their loot. After an inventory, it was found that over 200 yuan had been lost. The victim, Shi Fujin, reported the robbery to the County Court yesterday, requesting that the stolen goods be recovered and the bandits apprehended.

Li Gong's Corpse Verified to Have Fatal Injuries: Regarding the case of the unexplained death of Gong, the wife of Li Zhilin, a villager from Li Xiang, Yangshuyuan, Section 16 (Wan'an City), the Chief Judge Zhou and Prosecutor Du of the County Court, along with Xuan Fang, the coroner from the Wuxi County Local Court, exhumed Li Gong's body from her coffin at the Dongyue Temple in Huishan on the 28th for a re-examination. Due to the severe decomposition of the corpse, a thorough re-examination was impossible. Only a bone examination could be performed. Yesterday (29th) at 9:00 AM, Chief Judge Zhou and Prosecutor Du, along with Coroner Xuan and court police officers, traveled to the burial site by streetcar for the bone examination. The examination was completed at 2:00 PM. The bones were taken out and examined one by one. The bones with injuries were placed in a white basin, and Coroner Xuan examined them in detail. A red, fatal injury mark the size of a copper coin was found near the temple behind the right side of the head. Scraping with a bowl edge did not remove it. The seventh, eighth, and ninth ribs on the right side each had red injury marks. The seventh rib on the left side had a red injury mark. The left hip bone and back bone each had purplish-red injury marks. The entire right palm bone had red-black injury marks. The left tibia had two red marks, the right tibia had a red-flowered mark, and the right femur had a red mark. No other injuries were found. It was determined that the death was caused by injuries sustained before death. Chief Judge Zhou re-examined the findings and confirmed their accuracy. Li Zhilin was then brought to the scene to identify the injuries and was questioned. Li still denied the charges and claimed to be dissatisfied. Chief Judge Zhou ordered him to sign a statement and affix his fingerprint, and publicly announced that the injuries had been verified. The spectators applauded. Chief Judge Zhou ordered all the bones, injured and uninjured, to be taken to the court, pending Li Zhilin's appeal and review. The empty coffin was handed over to Jiang Zixian, the Tutouzheng of Huishan, for safekeeping. Li Zhilin was taken into custody by the court police. As for the witness Wu Jingwen, he asked Chief Judge Zhou on the spot what should be done with the judge and coroner who had conducted the previous examination. Judge Zhou replied that he had his own way of handling it and dismissed the matter.

Educational News

Important News

Ministry of Education Clarifies Graduation Qualifications of Advanced Academies

▲Treatment Equivalent to Specialized Schools under the Old System or Vocational Schools under the Current System

The Ministry of Education, in response to an inquiry regarding the graduation qualifications of advanced academies, sent a letter to the Examination Yuan, stating: "Based on the petition from Yao Wenzhi, a graduate of the Zhejiang Advanced Academy, requesting that his graduation qualifications be verified according to previous cases and approved for participation in higher examinations, your committee inquired and requested a reply. In response, the entrance requirements for advanced academies during the late Qing Dynasty were limited to middle school graduates, and the duration of study was set at three years, the same as preparatory courses at universities and advanced agricultural and commercial academies. The treatment of their graduates, such as being granted the status of Juren and various official positions, was also the same. These types of advanced agricultural and commercial academies were equivalent to specialized schools under the old system and vocational schools under the current system. Therefore, the advanced regular courses can be treated similarly. Upon verification, the graduate qualifications of this student should receive the same treatment as specialized schools under the old system or vocational schools under the current system. Furthermore, the Ministry previously approved the Ministry of Personnel's inquiry regarding the academic level of these academies, and ordered the Archives Preservation Office of the Ministry in Beiping to investigate and report the cases. Subsequently, the office submitted a list of these academies with attached explanations, which were consistent with the established cases. A written reply was sent in response. Now, based on the previous reasons, we are sending the list and explanations for your review and handling."

Ministry of Education Explains Qualifications of Teachers and Staff at Township Teacher Training Schools

The Ministry of Education, in response to a report from the Hubei Department of Education regarding whether teachers and staff at rural teacher training schools are qualified to serve as township school teachers, issued an instruction stating: "Graduates of senior high school normal courses should serve as primary school teachers. However, in practice in various provinces, some senior high school graduates serve as junior high school teachers. The first graduates of the provincial rural normal schools in the province have qualifications equivalent to senior high school graduates. Since they have served in rural teacher training schools for one year, if their performance is excellent and they have practical teaching experience, they may be allowed to serve as teachers in the first three years of the rural normal school. You should comply with this instruction."

Graduates from Unregistered Schools Outside This City Are Also Allowed to Take Entrance Exams

The Ministry of Education, in response to a report from the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau regarding whether graduates from unregistered private senior high schools outside this city should be allowed to take the entrance preliminary exams in this city, issued an instruction stating: "For entrance preliminary exams, graduates from unregistered private senior high schools that are not affiliated with the city should be allowed to take the exams together. You should be informed of this."

Preparatory News for the National Vocational Guidance Discussion Conference

The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute of the China Vocational Education Society is preparing to convene the National Vocational Guidance Discussion Conference, which will be held on August 1st and 2nd, concurrently with the National Vocational Education Discussion Conference, at Boxian Park in Zhenjiang. This has already been reported in this newspaper. The recent preparatory situation of the conference is extracted below:

▲Attending Representatives: The agencies that have recently registered to attend the conference include the Fujian Provincial Department of Education (Xu Taixian, Peng Chuanzhen), the Wujin Women's Vocational School of Jiangsu (Li Xiqi), the Nanyang Teachers' and Journalists' Introduction Agency (Huang Jingwan), the Provincial Nanjing Girls' Middle School (Tao Xuan, Wu Yuchang), the Provincial Taicang Middle School (Gu Zhongchao, Zheng Baoliang), Jinling University (Zhang Zhiwen), and Jinan University (Li Bangdong).

▲Proposed Motions: The institute has received many motions. After combining similar motions, the following important motions will be discussed: (1) A motion to encourage schools at all levels to establish more work-study positions; (2) A motion to connect with vocational circles to promote employment opportunities for graduates; (3) A motion to promote Northeast and Northwest reclamation groups to open new avenues for unemployed youth (the above three motions were proposed by the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute); (4) A motion to request the government to establish vocational training centers; (5) A motion to request the government to establish a national product sales office to develop new occupations (the above were proposed by the Changshu Poor Children's Home and the Changshu Vocational Guidance Institute); (6) A motion to request the Ministry of Education to instruct all provinces and cities to hire female teachers and staff as much as possible; (7) A motion to request the Ministry of Education to flexibly adjust the graduation deadlines for vocational courses in secondary schools to benefit students' employment (the above were proposed by the Shanghai Ai Qun Girls' Middle School).

▲Conference Schedule: The conference will participate in the opening ceremony of the National Vocational Education Discussion Conference on August 1st and attend the discussions. The Vocational Guidance Discussion Conference will be held on the morning of August 2nd at 9:00 AM. The schedule is as follows: (1) Formalities; (2) Opening remarks by Chairman Liu Zhanen, Gao Jiansi, and Jiang Wenyu; (3) Pan Yangyao reports on the progress of the conference; (4) Remarks by administrative officials and guests; (5) Expert speeches; (6) Discussion of motions.

Songjiang's Primary and Secondary Education Circles Fight for Education Funds

The Joint Association of Primary and Secondary School Teachers and Staff in Songjiang County held its second general meeting in the meeting hall of the County Education Association yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM. The chairman was Xu Renzun, and the recorder was Tang Zhenzhi. After the formalities, the chairman reported that the budget for various schools in the county for the 20th year had been arbitrarily reduced by the Department of Education, making it impossible to maintain operations. Taking tuition fees as an example, the original deduction for each class in urban primary schools was 48 yuan, but now the Department orders a deduction of 70 yuan per class, based on 35 students per class. The original deduction for each class in rural primary schools was 24 yuan, but now the Department orders a deduction of 56 yuan per class, based on 28 students per class. Primary school funding is already scarce, and now tuition fees are being deducted even further. The funding cuts for complete primary schools, middle schools, and normal schools are even greater. With such layers of exploitation, how can the primary and secondary school teachers and staff in the entire county bear this? The association has already sent telegrams to various agencies appealing for help. The original text of the telegram was read aloud. Next, the proposed motions were discussed: (1) What should be done if the funding for various schools in the 20th year is not fully resolved by the time school starts? It was resolved that, if necessary, the schools would jointly notify the students to postpone the start of school. (2) Set the date for the next meeting. It was decided that the next meeting would be held at 1:00 PM on August 5th at the County Education Association. It was also heard that if the authorities have not made any indication by the time of the next meeting, they plan to collectively petition the County Government.

Opening of the YMCA Summer School

The YMCA is holding a summer school for cadres in Lushan this year, as reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the summer school has opened in recent days. All teachers and students have arrived. The students attending the school represent YMCAs across the country, including Shenyang and Harbin in the Northeast, Xi'an and Taiyuan in the Northwest, Chongqing in Sichuan, and Fuzhou, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou in the South, totaling more than 50 people. The courses include "Sociology," "Religious Philosophy," "YMCA Administration," "Personality Education Methods," "Vocational Guidance," and "Rural Affairs," totaling more than 20 courses. Experts have been specially invited to serve as professors. The summer school will last for one month and is scheduled to close on August 20th. The school is located in the Yun Valley of Lushan, which has elegant scenery and perfect facilities, making it an ideal place for cadres to study, research, and rest during the summer.

New Normal School Established in Zhejiang Province

▲Renamed Hangzhou Normal School

A new provincial normal school has been established in Zhejiang Province. Since the Department of Education commissioned Zhang Yuannian to prepare for it, all internal matters, such as the formulation of organizations, the recruitment of teachers and staff, and the preparation of enrollment matters, have been arranged. It is certain that classes will begin in September. It is heard that the school was originally named Zhejiang Provincial Normal School by the Department of Education, but the official seal issued by the Provincial Government yesterday was named Zhejiang Provincial Hangzhou Normal School. The school will definitely follow the official seal issued by the province and change its name. Also, the school originally chose the old government school as its location, but the houses there are dilapidated and leaking, making them unsuitable for use. It is necessary to rebuild them. The construction project is estimated to take about half a year. Therefore, it is heard that in September, a large building on Henghe Bridge will be rented for use as a temporary school building.

Development of the Zhongda Business School

Since the Zhongda Business School in this port moved into its newly built buildings this spring, its scale has become larger and its facilities more complete. Currently, Mr. Xu Peikun is the president of the school. He has already decided on the direction of the school's recent development and has largely drafted the implementation plan, which will soon be available to the public. It is heard that Mr. Xu is extremely cautious in enriching and improving the curriculum and recruiting teachers. The professors who have been hired for the next semester are all scholars. Anyone with real talent and learning is recruited one by one. The number of applicants for new students this year is large, and the school's housing is insufficient, resulting in the temporary addition of a cool shed to accommodate more than a thousand people. The order during the examination was orderly. However, the examination curriculum for the new students in this class is different from previous years, attracting attention from all walks of life, and many people have asked questions. After President Xu's detailed explanation, he was finally understood. The special circumstances of this year's examination are briefly recorded below. In previous years, the Zhongda Business School's recruitment examinations always included economics and bookkeeping courses. However, all these courses were exempted from this year's examination. This is because students in different regions have different academic levels, and if these courses are tested, practical difficulties may arise. This is one of the reasons for the exemption. Secondly, when printing the enrollment brochure, the subject was not included. This is the second reason. However, at the same time, the examination for this year requires students to take biology, physics, and chemistry courses, which surprised all secondary school business students. This is because the existing secondary school business courses do not study these courses, so protests have been raised. After President Xu repeatedly reviewed the matter, he specially lowered the grading standards for this year's examination in order to avoid the regret of rejecting business students from afar. Seventy-one students have already been admitted. Today, advertisements have appeared in various newspapers, stating that these students must report to the Business School before September 1st. They must also take a group examination in English, Chinese, economics, and bookkeeping in order to be assigned to classes for lectures. In addition, President Xu pays special attention to the students' transfer process. If students request to transfer at any time and change their minds, they can show the weakness of the students' intentions. Therefore, he specifically stated to the new students in this class that they will not be transferred. If there are people who are interested in studying business, the Business School welcomes them very much. Those who have not yet made up their minds must think twice before acting.

Free Talk

World Briefs

— Sea Wanderer

The Electric Farm

The world's most modern farm is located in East Grinstead, on the border of Surrey and Sussex in England. The farm covers an area of 600 acres and is jointly owned by three people. The person in charge is Mr. B. Matthews, who has devoted his life to researching how to use electricity to assist in farm work. Thanks to his talents, he has managed to use electricity for 67 different purposes on this unique farm. Electricity is used to generate light and heat in each beehive. As a result, the bees can start working earlier each year, and each hive can produce 17 pounds more honey than usual. When calculated, this is a considerable amount. Electricity is also used for horse care, which saves a lot of labor. He has created a special machine that takes care of brushing and feeding the horses. Electricity is also used in the chicken coop to create a special clock. In winter, it emits light that gradually brightens, creating an artificial sunrise that is one hour earlier than the real sunrise. This makes the chickens healthier and able to produce more eggs. In addition, electricity is fully utilized for plowing, hatching, milking, haymaking, pest control, and other tasks, with very satisfactory results.

The Golden Bell Dog by the Sangzi River

— Li Xufan

It is the nature of dogs to guard homes. In modern times, due to the evolution of trends, more families are raising dogs. Humans use their keen senses and, based on the differences in their breeds, divide them into hunting dogs, police dogs, and racing dogs for training. Dogs also rely on their strengths to assist humans in their work. However, there is also a type of dog that, without being raised by humans, can fulfill the responsibility of guarding the night: the Golden Bell Dog. My friend, Mr. Zhao Huisan, recently returned to the south after resigning from the Guisui Railway Bureau. There were no fewer than twenty people traveling with him. Passing through the Sangzi River area, the mountains are stacked upon each other, and animal tracks are everywhere. Those accustomed to this place all carry tents and other equipment to camp along the way. Mr. Zhao also did the same. On a certain night, as the fish began to jump in the early hours, he was leaning against the tent inside, about to fall asleep. Suddenly, he heard footsteps approaching and pacing outside the tent. Suspecting that wild beasts were invading, he quickly called his companions to be on guard. Among them, one familiar with the local situation said, "Why are you so alarmed? Don't worry. The sound you hear is not from wild beasts. It is the Golden Bell Dogs patrolling in formation to drive away wolves and protect us." Mr. Zhao was half-doubtful, so he peeked out through the tent opening. Indeed, he saw groups of three to five yellow dogs, as tall as children and larger than ordinary dogs. Their eyes were bright and piercing, and their appearance was quite intimidating. He offered them bread and steamed buns, and they readily accepted the food. They did not avoid strangers, as if they were dogs raised in a household. Mr. Zhao laughed and said, "These are truly temporary guards who don't receive salaries!" The Golden Bell Dog is not only seen in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. It often inhabits the high mountains and forests of Suiyuan. Its four limbs are extremely sharp and it is good at jumping and skilled at overcoming wolves. When it sees a wolf, it will jump on its back. It immediately digs at the wolf's eyes with its sharp claws on its front feet, and it always hits its mark. It does not eat the defeated wolf. If it encounters a large number of wolves, the dog knows that it is outnumbered, so it barks loudly with a sound like a ringing bronze bell. Other dogs of its kind will gather in response to the sound and attack together across the mountains and fields, even reaching hundreds in number. They will not stop until the wolves flee in defeat or are wounded and killed. They have a strong spirit of loving the group and helping each other. Therefore, the Sangzi River area has a long route, inconvenient transportation, and steep mountains on both sides. Villages are extremely scarce, and wolves often appear there. Travelers often set up tents along the way to spend the night. Without the Golden Bell Dogs to guard the night, travelers would be hesitant and regard the area as a dangerous place. It can be seen that the Creator's creation of humans and things is truly unfathomable. This dog has the characteristic of resisting wolves and protecting humans, which is quite interesting to study. According to the locals, this dog is not raised by humans and likes to live in the wild. If people bring it back to raise it, it will become depressed and refuse to eat. Therefore, it cannot be kept as a domestic dog. Now, with Mr. Zhao's report, I will record it to share with readers.

Miss Universe

— Tao Zaidong

This newspaper's pictorial weekly on the 26th of this month published the representative beauties selected from various countries around the world this year. Recently, in a re-election held in Cowenston, USA, Ms. Du Shudi of Belgium was selected as the most beautiful among the beauties for her healthy physique and was honored with the title of Miss Universe. The original picture is there for all to see and appreciate. Seeing is believing, and opinions vary depending on one's perspective. From my perspective, I dare say she is not beautiful. If you cover her hair and shoes and look at her whole body, she has a very robust and extraordinary posture, vaguely concealing a threatening and intimidating air. She resembles Xiang Yu, the Hegemon-King of Chu, but unbelievably, she is Yu Ji. I like to nitpick words. In general, praising the femininity of a beauty always involves characters with the "woman" radical from the Kangxi dictionary, such as graceful, charming, enchanting, and beautiful. If you want to praise her health, like a female knight or female general, it is necessary to combine terms of strength and grace. Chinese and Western concepts are different. Now, the most beautiful among the beautiful is selected after repeated elections, and the judgment is based on the four words "healthy physique." It is like a comment from a physical education expert, boxer, or soldier, which seems ill-fitting for a young lady. It is like calling a man "slender," which a man would not appreciate. By analogy, a lady may not appreciate it either. I also like to worry on behalf of others. The universe encompasses the four directions and what is above and below. The cosmos encompasses the past and the present. With such a number one beauty, she may not adhere to the principle of remaining single. I ask, where can we find a Universe Young Master to pair her with? Alas, I have thought of one person. The warlord Hou Jing raised troops and called himself the "Universe General." When Emperor Wu of Liang saw the proclamation, he was shocked and said, "Does the General have the title of Universe?" If Ms. Du is willing to marry General Hou and act as his matchmaker, I would be pleased.

Snippets

— (Cuckoo)

Shi Yousan probably has rebellious bones. He is best at rebelling. He rebelled against Feng once, Jiang twice, and Yan three times. In three years, he rebelled three times in a row. The "You" character can be cut off at the head and changed to "Shi Fan San" (Shi Rebellious Three). Unexpectedly, he has recently been preparing troops and horses to rebel against Zhang. In that case, "Shi Yousan" should be changed to "Shi Fan Si" (Shi Rebellious Four). I only hope he stops here and does not continue to "rebel five" or "rebel six."

A Famous Dan and a Famous Play: Yutang Chun

— Gauze

From the late Qing Dynasty to the present, the past thirty years have witnessed an extraordinary development in opera, gradually becoming the national opera of the Republic of China. During this period, many famous actors have emerged, too numerous to mention. Since Mei Lanfang gained fame, the trend has changed again. What was once centered on male roles has transformed into being centered on female roles. The title of "King of the Opera World" belongs not to male leads but to female leads. Famous female leads have emerged one after another, resulting in the so-called "Four Great Golden Kang" Mei (Lanfang), Cheng (Yanqiu), Shang (Xiaoyun), and Xun (Huisheng). Male leads have become increasingly weak, mostly becoming appendages of famous female leads. Moreover, there are more than just these famous female leads. In addition to the Four Great Golden Kang, there are also Xu Biyun and female actor Xue Yanqin, who can each lead their own forces. There are also the Southern Four Golden Kang: Xiao Yang Yuelou, Liu Xiaoheng, Wang Yunfang, and Zhao Junyu, who also possess considerable accomplishments. Their influence is truly great. With so many famous female leads, naturally, female-led operas are more fashionable than male-led operas. In addition to the new operas arranged by each famous female lead, many old operas are also very popular. The most fashionable of the old operas is Yutang Chun. Each famous female lead attaches great importance to this opera. Every time they come south to Shanghai, they perform it several times, and each performance always sells out. It can be seen how enthusiastic the public is. Xun Huisheng is especially popular for this opera. Xu Biyun also staged a prequel, Yutang Chun, using the three words "Yutang Chun" as a gimmick. Not long ago, Mei Lanfang performed for three nights at the Grand Theatre to raise funds for the Jiangxi flood disaster, and one of the nights was Yutang Chun. Given this situation, it is not an exaggeration to say that Yutang Chun is the first famous opera. Now, let's talk about the opera Yutang Chun itself. The plot of this opera is based on true events. It was originally Qinqiang opera, but it was changed to Peking opera at the end of the Qing Dynasty, hence the name "New Yutang Chun." However, most of the lyrics are still from the original version. Therefore, there are many places where the rhyme scheme does not match. I remember that this publication once carried a manuscript discussing this between Tianxu Wosheng and a certain gentleman, but I can't remember the details completely. Everyone probably knows the places where the rhyme scheme does not match, so there is no need to list them. I will only talk about the reason why the rhyme scheme does not match in this opera. Originally, Jin people spoke with a nasal tone, and the "Dong" and "Zhen" rhymes were easily confused. For example, "Hunyuan Prefecture" was pronounced "Hongyuan Prefecture" by Jin people. There was little difference between "Hong" and "Hun." Once it was changed to Peking opera, using the Central Plains rhyme, the rhyme scheme no longer matched. At the time, when it was first changed to Peking opera, why didn't anyone notice this and just swallowed it whole, resulting in a flaw in the famous opera? It is truly regrettable. The two characters "Hongdong" are even more confusing. I don't know that this opera is based on true events. It is neither Hongtong nor Hongtong. The correct name is Hongdong, which is an oblique tone, not a level tone. During the Zhou Dynasty, Hongdong was the state of the Marquis of Yang. During the Northern Qi Dynasty, it was Hongdong Town. During the Sui Dynasty, it was Hongdong County, and it has continued to be so to this day. During the Ming and Qing Dynasties, it belonged to Pingyang Prefecture in Shanxi. In the early years of the Republic of China, when administrative regions were reorganized, it belonged to the Hedong Street in Shanxi. The files of the Yutang Chun case are still preserved in the Hongdong County Government. You can see them for a dollar. So, why are people today confused about the current county name? It is indeed a strange thing. Furthermore, the reason why this opera can become a famous opera is because famous female leads have popularized it. However, in my opinion, just performing the three trials is only one scene from beginning to end, which is extremely simple. However, it takes no less than forty-five minutes to an hour to sing. It is very tiring for the performer, and the audience also finds it unbearable. It can be considered an extremely difficult opera to please the audience. Yet, it has become so popular, which is puzzling.

▲ News from the Art World: Novelist Zhang Zhenyuan is also skilled in cursive script. He previously collaborated with Ma Henian on a calligraphy and painting fan exhibition, which sold out instantly. Later visitors had nothing to buy, so starting yesterday, another exhibition was opened at the Liangchen Haoyou Society on Beijing Road for ten days. The items displayed this time are all gold-faced, with Zhang Zhenyuan's double-lined cursive script, self-recorded from his original novels. The details of the green landscape paintings that Mr. Ma collaborated on are even more elaborate. Each item is sold cheaply for five yuan. (Birun)

Miscellaneous Notes on American Women's Lives (4)

— Sent

▲ Career: American women's education has equal opportunities with men. In their careers, women also tend to progress together with men. After leaving school, those who are poor are indeed eager to find a career to maintain their livelihood. Even those who are wealthy do not want to enjoy life at home but are willing to serve in society. They believe that a woman who has received an education and does not serve the public has lost the purpose of education. Failing to find a career exposes women's weaknesses and is a sign of women's incompetence, which is also very shameful. There are also many women whose husbands hold superior positions and have abundant income, but they still want to find work. They are hardworking and can endure hardship. Even if they work outside during the day, they still handle household affairs as usual, as few small families hire servants. The most common career for women is as shop clerks. In large and small businesses in various cities, their presence can be seen everywhere. According to my (Dr. Qian's self-proclaimed) observation, their service performance is better than men, such as: (1) agile movements (2) clear minds (3) polite to people. Second, typists, secretaries in government offices, nurses in hospitals, kindergarten nannies, primary and secondary school teachers... etc., are the biggest outlets for women. In addition, those who graduate from university graduate schools and engage in independent professions include doctors, lawyers, accountants, and university professors. Almost all men's careers have been partially occupied by women.

▲ Political Participation: Women's nature is gentle, and their魄力 and decisiveness are naturally not comparable to men. Therefore, the number of women active on the political stage in various countries is still small. The history of women's political participation in the United States is relatively long. As far as I know, the highest political position for women in the United States is that two of the forty-eight state governors are women. There are also many women in the state government's secretary-general and senior political officials. There are also several mayors who are women. There are even more female judges. Among the female judges of the Supreme Court in Ohio (Ohio), women also occupy a seat. It can be seen that women's political participation in the United States is more developed than in other countries. Also, during parliamentary elections, they compete fiercely. However, it is not for their own sake but for the number of seats for women or for the number of votes for female candidates. Based on the current situation, it is reasonable to be infinitely optimistic about their future in political participation. (The End)

Rotary Club Fiction

Woman, Woman (4)

— Yao Sufeng

Mr. Lu walked out of the Ding's residence, his joyful expression replaced by a hurried look. Thinking about the conversation he had just had with Miss Ding, he felt it was indeed his best work; but how would he deal with tomorrow's appointment? Counting the money in his pocket, he had only two dollars left. Needless to say, buying a valuable gift was not permitted by reality. Even buying a decent bouquet of flowers would make him hesitate.

He returned to the school, where the dormitory during the holidays was truly desolate. He alone assessed his future fate, as if boundless light were surrounded by heavy clouds. The more he thought, the more distant and empty he felt. Finally, he spent an unavoidable night in a hot dream of vagueness and emptiness.

When he woke up, it was not yet dawn. But he had finally decided on his final plan. He couldn't sleep anymore. Calculating that there was still time to catch the early train, he hurriedly put on his clothes, didn't wash his face, didn't fold his quilt, didn't take anything, and hurried to the train station.

Bags, baskets, boxes, and people filled the carriages of the third-class train. He was just a lone individual. He accidentally heard the hawkers selling their wares on the platform, and finally remembered that his mother had told him to buy some bananas when he went back. He painfully spent the remaining forty cents to buy a bunch of bananas as the only gift he would bring home.

Suzhou had arrived. Looking out of the train window at the towering North Temple Pagoda, it still proudly looked down on this unimproved ancient city. Only the complex sounds of people and horses outside the station clearly indicated their urgent expectations. Mr. Lu was reluctant to hear the shouting of many coachmen soliciting customers, because it seemed that he would always feel an unusual sense of shame and resentment in his own mind.

His home was not far from the station. He carried the only bunch of bananas and walked slowly. But many coachmen were disappointed, because in their initial psychology, a foreign-dressed guest from Shanghai like this could at least earn more fare money.

The scenery remained the same. A burst of dog barking chased Mr. Lu to his own home. When he saw his own gate, he only felt annoyance. He only silently prayed that this time when he had to return, he would not have to return unavoidably again!

"Xiao Rong! Is that you? Wearing foreign clothes, you look like a different person!" When Mr. Lu stepped into the gate, the young clerk standing by the door was stunned. His seemingly surprised tone made Mr. Lu have to lower his head and gently ask, "Is Dad at home?"

"What a coincidence! Today our carriage didn't go to catch the early train business. He's probably inside. Speaking of which, they've been looking forward to you for a long time. How come you only thought of coming home today?" the young clerk said happily.
