Good American Cotton Harvest Estimated

The National Society telegraphed from New York on the 28th: It is estimated here that the American cotton harvest this year will reach 14 million bales. The cost of production is estimated to be 14 cents per pound, but if there is no major improvement in the current market situation, the new cotton will only be sold for 9 cents per pound after it enters the market.

Grain: Sunny Weather Causes Rice Market to Plummet by One Yuan

▲Xinzha: Yesterday, the supply from the west road was still surging, and transactions for various goods were extremely sluggish. Due to the sunny weather, there were few buyers from various shops, and sentiment was weak. Hou Geng and Zaowan Dao (early and late rice) fell by 4-5 jiao. There was little interest in Lu Yang Jian and Bian Yin Yuan, so prices dropped by 3 jiao. However, the Bu Jian goods were scarce, and prices remained at the original level. According to a survey at 4-5 o'clock yesterday along the Suzhou River, there were a total of over 260 boats, with an average of 90 shi per boat, totaling approximately 23,400 dan of Bai Geng and Xian rice.

▲Nanshi: There were about 20 source firms from various gangs. Due to the sunny weather, city and rural shops reduced their purchasing interest, and commission purchases were also thin. There were very few buyers in the market, and sentiment was downwards. The Hou Geng market price plummeted by one yuan compared to yesterday. There was still a large accumulation of early and thin rice, and there were no transactions with guest firms. The local sales were limited, and prices also fell by 6-7 jiao. There was a lack of appetite for Yang Lu Jian goods, and the situation remained stable. Bian Hua sales were average, and there was no rise or fall. Few guest Jian rice arrived, so the trend continued to weaken.

Flour Market Opens High and Stays High

▲Gangs from the Yangtze River and Inland Areas Competing to Purchase

Yesterday, the flour market initially fluctuated. Due to the continuing good weather, foreign wheat also fluctuated by one or two jiao. The market sentiment was very flat. However, after the second session, it became increasingly popular because gangs from the inland and Yangtze River areas felt that the heavy floods would be difficult to control for a while, the price of grain would skyrocket, and famine was inevitable. Therefore, buyers remained eager, competing to purchase both near and far terms. As a result, sentiment was excited, and prices opened high and stayed high. The near-term market was particularly popular due to factory restrictions. For the far-term market, Fufeng sold about 200,000, slightly easing the situation. As a result, this month rose by 2.5 fen compared to the previous day, August rose by 2.75 li, September rose by 2.5 fen, October rose by 1.75 li, November rose by 2 fen, and December rose by 1.5 fen.

Manipulation and Speculation in the Wheat Market

▲Near-Term Rose by One Qian... Far-Term Slightly Declined

Yesterday, there was a sudden and significant change in the wheat market. The opening in the morning was relatively stable. Later, the inland gangs, aware of the disastrous floods and interrupted transportation, realized that the supply of wheat would definitely be affected. Therefore, while foreign wheat could still be delivered in the far term, only local wheat could be used in the near term. As a result, they absorbed as much as possible to prepare for manipulation and speculation. The famine has not yet occurred, but speculators immediately raised prices. The instability of domestic grain prices is a major concern for people's food supply. The opening price in the afternoon had already risen covertly, and later it rose even more sharply, with a difference of 3 fen compared to the previous day's closing price. The far-term market, due to concerns about foreign wheat, saw a slight drop in price increases. As a result, August rose by 1 qian, September rose by 7 fen, October rose by 6 fen, November rose by 4 fen, and December rose by 3 fen. Due to the scarcity of spot wheat and the interruption of the supply source, asking prices also rose by 3-4 fen. Over 2,000 packages of wheat from Kunshan, Anting, Chongming, Zhenjiang, Chuzhou, Penglai, and Waigang were purchased by Fuxin and Huafeng.

Silk and Tea: Tunxi Zhenmei Active Sales to France

Yesterday, in the local foreign tea market, British firm Xiehe Yanghang expressed a strong interest in Tunxi, Shexian, and Suian Zhenmei green teas due to receiving overseas demand. Jinlong and Tongfu and other firms also actively searched for supplies. The total transaction volume in the city reached over 2,500 boxes, making it the most active trading in recent times. However, there were still no large-scale sales of Wuyuan Gaozhuang Zhenmei. The market for Zhunmei and Xiumei goods became increasingly firm. Shrimp Eye Pearl Tea also saw slightly more sales than before. The overall trend of the tea market showed signs of firm stability.

New Silkworm Cocoon Waste from Hangzhou and Shaoxing Continues to be Shipped to Shanghai

Yesterday, 240 dan of new silkworm cocoon waste from Hangzhou and Shaoxing were shipped to Shanghai. The market remained popular.

European firms were eager to suppress prices and hoard supplies, while Chinese silk merchants refused to sell at a loss. The market was quiet, and no transactions were reported.

Dried and Fresh Goods: New Fuzhou Yuanhong Lychees Have Arrived

▲Selling Price Approximately 100 Taels

Yuanhong lychees produced in Fuzhou, with small seeds, thick flesh, and exceptional sweetness, have always been known as a famous product. This year's output was very low, and land prices were high. Fresh fruits had already entered the market early. However, since dried fruits need to be sun-dried and fire-roasted, the first batch of goods only arrived in Shanghai yesterday, totaling over 200 boxes. Half of them were being transshipped to other ports, and half were self-operated by merchants. It is reported that the cost is approximately 130 yuan, and the estimated selling price should be around 100 taels, but the market has not yet been fully established.

Local News

Today's Mass Meeting

▲Held at 3 PM

▲At the Public Sports Ground

Various sectors of the city, in order to arouse the people to strive for the same goal, have initiated the "Suppress Bandits, Punish Rebels, Resist Japan, and Aid Overseas Chinese" civic assembly. With the permission of the city party headquarters, it is scheduled to be held at the Public Sports Ground in the South City at 3 PM today. This afternoon, all public organizations and factories (except for public transport) will have a half-day holiday to facilitate participation. All assembly staff have been appointed by the preparatory committee, and the venue has been fully decorated by workers hired by the preparatory committee yesterday.

The city executive committee issued a notice yesterday: "Regarding the notice, the city's Preparatory Committee for the 'Suppress Bandits, Punish Rebels, Resist Japan, and Aid Overseas Chinese Assembly' has submitted a request that at this time of internal and external difficulties, the entire citizenry should express enthusiasm for suppressing the red bandits, punishing the rebel Shi, and resolutely implementing economic severance with Japan, and plans to convene a civic assembly at the Public Sports Ground in the South City at 3 PM on the 30th of this month to serve as a backing for the government, requesting approval for the record and notifying all factories to cease work and participate, etc. This committee has approved the record. Therefore, this emergency notice is issued to all factories in the city: except for workers in transportation, public utilities, and news services, who should have representatives designated by their respective labor unions to participate while continuing to work as usual, all others should cease work for half a day on the afternoon of the 30th, with workers allowed to participate with full pay. This notice is hereby issued."

French Concession Public Court Officially Taken Over on the 1st

▲Liang Renjie, President of the Third High Court Branch

▲Ying Shi, President of the Second Special District Court

▲Improving the Management Methods of Prisons

The case of recovering the Shanghai French Concession Public Court has been completed through negotiations between representatives of the Chinese and French governments. The agreement on the recovery of the Public Court was formally signed on the 28th of this month by representatives of both sides at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing. The full text of the agreement consists of 14 articles and one exchange of letters. The content and methods are roughly the same as the agreement for the Public Concession. At the same time, the Ministry of Justice issued instructions, and Xu Weizhen, President of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court, specially ordered Yang Zhaojun, President of the Shanghai First Special District Local Court, to prepare to be responsible for the takeover. On the French side, the Consul in Shanghai also ordered the Public Court to prepare to officially hand over on August 1st. The organization and personnel after the Public Court is taken back, as well as the takeover procedures and subsequent reforms, are separately recorded below:

▲Organization after Recovery: The Ministry of Justice has decided on the organization after the recovery of the French Public Court, reorganizing the original Public Court into the Shanghai Second Special District Local Court, and establishing the Jiangsu Third Higher Branch Court as an appellate body to fully comply with the Chinese judicial system. Because the Public Court only has two tribunals, which is insufficient to handle cases, it has been decided to add two more tribunals. However, there will be no distinction between civil, criminal, and enforcement designations. In addition, because the original buildings are insufficient for office space, seven buildings have been rented opposite the Public Court in He Mei Fang to serve as the Second Special District Local Court. Six buildings have also been rented in Heng Ai Li on Avenue de President Conty to serve as the office of the Third Higher Branch Court.

▲Selection of Personnel for the Two Courts: The Ministry of Justice has selected several judges with excellent character and learning from the courts of various provinces to serve as presidents and presiding judges of the reorganized courts. According to this newspaper's reporter, it has been internally determined that the position of President of the Third Higher Branch Court will be filled by Liang Renjie, President of the Jiangxi Higher Court, and the position of President of the Second Special District Local Court will be filled by Ying Shi, Presiding Judge of the Civil Tribunal of the First Special District Court of the Public Concession. It is reported that the position of Chief Prosecutor of the Third Higher Branch Court will be filled by Qian Qian, Chief Prosecutor of the Hubei Higher Court. The selection of personnel for the positions of presiding judge of the two courts is still underway, but it is said that Zhou Han, Presiding Judge of the First Special District Local Court, may be transferred. As for the number of judges, it has been internally determined to be six to eight, and the selection of personnel is also underway. However, according to reliable sources, Zhou Renda of the First Special District Court has been decided to be transferred to serve as a judge of the Second Court. The above personnel selections will be officially announced as soon as the takeover is completed.

▲Prisons Must Be Reformed: According to news from the Shanghai judicial authorities, the content of the agreement to recover the French Public Court is the same as that of the Public Concession, but the French side has completely returned the right to manage prisons to China, unlike the agreement for the Public Concession, where the right to manage prisons remains in the hands of foreigners. The Shanghai judicial authorities believe that the original management methods of the French Public Court prison have many shortcomings, such as: (1) small space and overcrowding, which does not conform to hygiene; (the original prison initially had one person per room, which was later increased to three people per room); (2) overly strict management, which violates humanitarianism; (3) religious methods are used to teach and guide prisoners, with only a few priests providing instruction, which seems unlikely to be effective; (4) work and rest are not adjusted, and the ability of prisoners is not considered, forcing them to engage in hard labor, such as forcing intellectuals to do hard labor, which seems inappropriate, and the rewards given are also very few. After the recovery, the above points must be reformed, and modifications will also be made to the prison buildings. More than one hundred experienced and capable managers from prisons in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, and other provinces will be sent to Shanghai to fill these positions. This group of personnel will arrive in Shanghai in the coming days, and more than ninety pairs of leather shoes and one hundred and ninety sets of uniforms have been made for use.

▲Insufficient Funding: After the recovery and reorganization of the French Public Court, the recurring expenses should also be increased because it is larger than before. The court itself only has an annual income of approximately 200,000 yuan. After the reorganization, the expenses of the two courts will be at least 30,000 yuan per month (the two courts require several tens of thousands of yuan per month, and the prison requires 7,000 yuan per month). Based on an annual calculation, at least 400,000 yuan is needed, which is twice the court’s own income. It is reported that after the establishment, the Ministry of Justice will allocate subsidies to cover this shortfall.

▲Takeover Set for the 1st: President Yang of the First Special District Court informally met with French Consul Ganglin the day before yesterday. Ganglin stated that he had ordered the French Public Court to hand over everything on Saturday (August 1st) and that all expenses for the prison would cease from August 1st. Yang traveled to Beijing that evening and returned to Shanghai on the 30th. President Yang is preparing to officially take over on August 1st and has scheduled a meeting with Ganglin today to discuss the takeover procedures. President Yang stated that he will actively prepare after the takeover and expects to officially establish the court on August 16th. If preparations are not completed in time, the establishment must be announced by September 1st at the latest.

▲French Consul Travels to Beijing: The French Consul-General, Ganglin, and the negotiation committee member were playing in Putuo, and because the continuous rains were too heavy, the Consul was unable to arrive in Beijing as scheduled when the Public Court agreement was signed the day before yesterday. He only returned to Shanghai from Putuo the night before last. Because the agreement had to be published immediately after signing, Ganglin arrived in Shanghai the night before last and took a China National Aviation Corporation plane to Beijing at 7 AM yesterday, arriving in Nanjing at 9:15 AM yesterday. He went to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to complete the signing (New Sound News Agency).

▲Full Text Announced: After the French Consul went to Beijing to complete the signing yesterday morning, both sides announced the full text of the agreement that afternoon. The agreement stipulates that the effective period is three years, from August 1, 1931 (the 20th year of the Republic of China), to July 31, 1934 (the 23rd year of the Republic of China). All Shanghai French Public Courts and the regulations and ordinances related to the Public Courts will be abolished when the agreement takes effect (i.e., August 1st) (New Sound News Agency).

Minister Song Denies the Rights to Guangdong Bonds

▲Notice to Chinese and Foreign Merchants

Finance Minister Song Ziwen of the National Government issued a notice yesterday: "Regarding the notice, the domestic and foreign debts and reparations borne by customs duties, and the funds allocated for unsecured domestic and foreign debts, are secured by the entire national customs duties, and are not mortgaged by any specific part. All national customs duties, regardless of which part, are obligated to compensate for domestic and foreign debts and reparations. At present, the so-called old portion of customs duties collected by national customs is only sufficient to pay off foreign debts and reparations. Now, the Guangdong rebels have withheld all the new portion of customs duties collected by the customs offices in Guangdong and Guangxi, using it for their own purposes, and plan to issue prize bonds secured by the duties. These acts not only hinder the integrity of the customs but also deprive the vested rights of the bondholders secured by the customs duties. Therefore, this notice is to inform all Chinese and foreign banks, merchants, and people that all prize bonds or other bonds issued by the Guangdong rebels, whether secured by all or part of the customs duties, are invalid. The National Government will under no circumstances recognize that such bonds have any right to claim repayment of principal or interest from the central treasury's past, present, or future income. This notice is hereby issued."

Song Ziwen, Minister of Finance of the National Government.

Anti-Japanese and Aid-Overseas-Chinese Conference Decides on Measures for Handling Japanese Goods

▲Collect Relief Funds for Japanese Goods Before the 24th

▲All Japanese Goods Found After the 24th Will Be Confiscated

New Work in the Midst of the Anti-Japanese and Aid-Overseas-Chinese Movement

▲Commercial Association's Notice: To whom it may concern, this time economic severance with Japan should be automatically organized by the business community. As this city is the focus of national attention, it should be the first to advocate and comply with the principle of automatic organization, etc. Our factory is one of the city's domestic goods factories and should join the movement. Therefore, over the years, we have spared no expense to painstakingly research and use the latest electric machines to meticulously weave 320-needle to 360-needle domestic Guo Fu brand silk dancing socks and various kinds of men's and women's silk and thread socks. We have long enjoyed the support of merchants both in and outside of this city, who have actively purchased and promoted our products. We are also grateful for the praise and advocacy of all sectors, which has encouraged us to work harder and strive for perfection to repay the concern of all sectors for domestic products. Now, for the sake of aiding overseas Chinese and resisting Japan, we hope that all sectors will exert their utmost sincerity to strive for the final survival of the nation. All employees and workers of our factory unanimously refuse to purchase Japanese goods. To facilitate the purchase of domestic goods, we have specially established a distribution office and retail store at 195 Guangxi Road, offering various products at greatly reduced prices regardless of cost. A wide variety of colors and styles are on display. Patriotic comrades are welcome to visit and inspect, and we will serve you sincerely.

Cheng Yu Xin Tea House

The Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Committee, regarding the disposal of Japanese goods, during its third Executive Committee meeting, based on a proposal by Design Committee member Chen Songyuan, appointed Tao Baichuan, Zhu Yingpeng, Li Wenjie, Yu Hualong, Fang Jiaobo, and other five committee members to jointly review the matter. Yesterday, the Review Committee finalized its review report and submitted it to the fourth Executive Committee meeting for approval. From now on, all Japanese goods will be handled accordingly. Details are as follows:

▲Disposal Measures: The fourth Executive Committee meeting was held at 5:00 PM yesterday. Over twenty Executive Committee members attended. Wang Xiaolai was publicly elected as chairman to discuss the review report on the disposal of Japanese goods submitted by the Review Committee. The following resolutions were passed: (A) The disposal of Japanese goods should be divided into three steps: (1) For Japanese goods paid for by merchants and stored before July 14th, they should be registered with the committee within the registration period. Upon completion of registration, certificates will be issued allowing their sale without charge. However, if Japanese goods paid for by merchants and stored before July 14th are transported and sold without registration, and are discovered by this committee, an anti-Japanese aid-to-overseas-Chinese relief fund of 10% of the value will be collected, and registration will be supplemented. (2) For Japanese goods paid for by merchants and stored between July 14th and July 24th, they should be registered with the committee within the registration period. At the time of registration, an anti-Japanese aid-to-overseas-Chinese relief fund equivalent to 10% of the loan value will be collected. Upon completion of registration, certificates will be issued allowing their sale. However, if Japanese goods paid for by merchants and stored between July 14th and July 24th are transported and sold without registration, and are discovered by this committee, an anti-Japanese aid-to-overseas-Chinese relief fund will be collected at twice the rate, and registration will be supplemented. (3) For those who purchase and transport Japanese goods after July 24th, all goods discovered will be confiscated. Even if the purchased goods were purchased before July 24th but are not registered with the committee within the specified time, they will also be confiscated if discovered. (B) After registration of each item, various trade associations should store them in one or two warehouses and send a letter to this committee. The committee will, together with the Chamber of Commerce, send personnel to inspect and verify them clearly. Each item will be marked with a seal separately, allowing it to be transported and sold. If export is desired, the relevant trade association can send a letter to this committee to apply for a permit. The permit will be stamped and issued by this committee together with the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for mutual verification. After the goods arrive, the recipient should first report to the local anti-Japanese association and chamber of commerce for inspection and registration before they can be picked up. In the future, if any unregistered goods are found, they should be detained and confiscated as anti-Japanese aid-to-overseas-Chinese relief funds. It was further resolved that the following information should be clearly stated in the registration form under the remarks section: (1) Goods marks, (2) Numbers, (3) Warehouse where stored.

▲Design Meeting: The Design Committee of the association held its first meeting yesterday. Committee members Chen Songyuan, Li Wenjie, Xu Yongzuo, Kui Yanfang, Pan Xulun, Chen Haiqiu, Zhou Jingzhai, Wu Zhihao, Zhu Wenqi, and Xue Guangqian attended. The following resolutions were passed: (1) Request the government to order the Customs Administration to clearly indicate the country of origin when importing foreign goods to prevent Japanese people from fraudulently claiming other origins. (2) Establish a coordination committee as soon as possible. (3) Regarding industrial raw materials and daily necessities that cannot be replaced in practice, standards should be established first. This matter should be handled by the association sending a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to establish a research committee for resisting Japanese goods as soon as possible, to conduct detailed research and establish standards, and then submit them to the association for reference. (4) Japanese goods that have been seized and paid for before July 14th should be handled according to the registration measures. (5) This association should immediately, together with the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, invite representatives from various industries, and also invite hometown associations and the Red Cross, which are related to overseas Chinese, to quickly raise donations to provide relief and condolences. (6) Invite those with expertise in diplomacy from the anti-Japanese association to set up a diplomatic research committee to study countermeasures against Japan and provide them to the diplomatic authorities. (7) Telegraph the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications to expedite the transportation of domestic coal and Chinese raw materials to reduce the import of Japanese coal. (8) Discussed the opinions of Committee Members Chen Songyuan and Kui Yanfang. It was resolved that the above eight proposals were all passed and recommended to the Executive Committee. (9) Appointed Committee Members Li Wenjie and Zhu Wenqi to draft the association's organizational charter. It was resolved and passed. (10) Decided to hold the third meeting at 1:00 PM on Saturday, convened by Committee Member Li Wenjie. It was resolved and passed.

▲For His Opposition to Inspecting Japanese Goods

The National Society stated that the Third District Branch of the Kuomintang and various trade associations in this city voiced their opposition to the remarks made by Mr. Feetham, Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession. The original text is recorded as follows:

▲Declaration of the Third District Branch: Recently, we read in the "Shanghai Evening Post and Mercury" a statement by Mr. Feetham, Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession, in which he considered our people's boycott of Japanese goods illegal and stated that he had ordered the police to strictly suppress it. This is incomprehensible. We have observed that Japanese imperialists have spared no effort in their aggression and oppression against our country. Recently, the Wanpaoshan incident, in which our people's land was forcibly occupied, and the instigation to massacre overseas Chinese, have particularly aroused the boiling blood and indignation of our countrymen. Therefore, people from all walks of life have expressed their patriotic enthusiasm and voluntarily organized the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Committee to advocate permanent economic severance with Japan. The inspection and detention of Japanese goods are naturally necessary actions during the period of economic severance. Now, Mr. Feetham not only fails to support our citizens' legitimate actions with justice but instead considers them illegal and further interferes and suppresses them. His absurdity has reached this point, which shows that British and Japanese imperialists are birds of a feather. The May 30th Massacre is a clear proof of this. Although a weak country has no diplomacy to speak of, fortunately, our people's spirit is boiling and sufficient to break through the sky. If Mr. Feetham implements his absurd suppression actions, then our Chinese citizens will only turn their determination against Japan and apply it to Britain. We hope that Mr. Feetham can wake up and automatically correct his mistakes so that Chinese-British friendship will not be broken. Otherwise, although our country is weak, our people's spirit is not diminished, and we will lead the citizens to deal with him with severe means. This is our declaration. Please be informed. Executive Committee of the Third District Branch of the Kuomintang of Shanghai Special Municipality.

Distressed Overseas Chinese Who Suffered in Korea Arrive in Shanghai

▲Painfully Narrating the Circumstances of the Massacre of Overseas Chinese

▲The Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Association Repatriates Them

The Nissho Kyodo Maru, departing from Incheon, Korea, to Yantai, carried twenty-five distressed overseas Chinese on the previous day. After arriving, they transferred to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xinming Lun and arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday morning. They are temporarily staying at the Wanshun Inn in Xinkaihe. Yesterday afternoon, the distressed overseas Chinese went to the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Association in this city to request relief. According to them, on the day of the incident, they were residing in the countryside of Incheon when they suddenly saw overseas Chinese residing in the city fleeing to the countryside. At the same time, stray bullets were

Page 14

flying in all directions, so they fled together. According to overseas Chinese in the city, Japanese guards also participated in the shooting at the time. More than forty people fled with us, and about four or five people were lost along the way. When boarding the ship, several names were scattered again. Among these twenty-five people, fourteen are from the business community, and the rest are farmers. The Anti-Japanese Association negotiated with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to obtain twenty-five free tickets and issued subsidies to repatriate them. They will probably leave Shanghai by ship tonight. The full list of the twenty-five distressed overseas Chinese is recorded below: Ding Qizhang, 28 years old, Ding Yushan, 36 years old, Ma Yueting, 27 years old, Peng Licai, 22 years old, Qiu Hongkuan, 41 years old, Liu Yunhuan, 26 years old, He Mingli, 48 years old, Deng Mingde, 26 years old, Li Yunjie, 17 years old, Ms. Zhang, 37 years old, two children. All of the above are from Huangpi County, Hankou, Hubei. Li Yuebo, 43 years old, Lv Zhongyan, 28 years old, Lv Yongru, 12 years old, Ms. Lv, 51 years old, Wang Shoudong, 72 years old, Chu Lianke, 49 years old, Mei Yongcai, 35 years old. The above people will go to Hankou, Nanjing, and other places respectively. There are also four unnamed men and women from Guangji County and one unnamed person from Xindu County, Sichuan.

Madam Soong's Coffin Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

▲Soong Tzu-wen and Others Arrive on the Ship Together

▲Reburial to Take Place in One or Two Weeks

Minister of Finance Soong Tzu-wen, accompanied by his sons Tzu-liang and Tzu-an, and others, arrived on the customs cruiser Haihsing with Madam Soong's coffin from Qingdao yesterday morning at 7:10 AM at the Taikoo Wharf.

Coffin of Madam Soong is Transported from Ship to Vehicle (Photographed by Our Newspaper)

Madam Soong's coffin was immediately transported to the Soong residence on Seymour Road for temporary placement and to begin the mourning ceremonies. Mourners are arriving in droves, and carriages are constantly coming and going. The details of the coffin's arrival in Shanghai are recorded as follows:

▲Wharf Security: Around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, over a hundred Annamite soldiers and the entire team of Chinese and Western detectives were dispatched by the French police to the vicinity of the Taikoo Wharf to maintain security and drive away idlers. The intelligence team of the Garrison Headquarters and armed police officers from the Public Security Bureau stood at the entrances and exits of the wharf with guns, creating a serious atmosphere. Those entering and exiting in plain clothes were required to wear funeral badges, effectively turning the area into a special zone. The Municipal Bureau sent a team of soldiers, and Director Chen Xizeng was on the scene to direct everything. In addition, Huang Renlin, the director-general of the Nanjing Lishi Society, and others came to Shanghai to assist with the arrangements.

▲Family Welcoming: At 6:40 AM, Minister of Industry Kong Xiangxi, accompanied by his wife Soong Ai-ling, and Madam Chiang Soong Mei-ling, Madam Soong Tzu-wen, and their children, arrived at the Taikoo Wharf in separate cars. Kong was wearing a Xia cloth long gown with a black armband. Madam Soong Mei-ling and her sisters, as well as their children, were all wearing black cloth robes, black gauze stockings, and black gauze shoes, with sorrowful expressions. Because it was still early, the ladies rested in the cars for a while. Before long, Mayor Zhang and his wife also arrived together.

▲Haihsing Arrives: At 6:50 AM, the customs cruiser Haihsing, all in gray, with black smoke billowing, was clearly visible. A mournful melody was played simultaneously, as if lamenting. Madam Soong Mei-ling and others rushed to the wharf, lined up, and gazed from afar. As the cruiser passed, all Chinese and foreign vessels in the river lowered their flags to half-mast to show their condolences. It was not until 7:10 AM that it docked properly.

Family Members Line Up to Greet at the Wharf (Photographed by Our Newspaper)

▲Prayers on the Ship: At that time, Minister of Finance Soong Tzu-wen, dressed in Western attire with a black armband, was leaning against the deck and nodding to the Kong family and others. Madam Soong's coffin was at the rear of the ship, surrounded by wreaths. Soon after, Madam Soong Mei-ling and others boarded the ship, along with the pastor who accompanied Soong and members of the church. They held a prayer service on the ship for about ten minutes.

▲Coffin Transported Ashore: The Wan Guo Funeral Parlor was responsible for the coffin's transportation. A large car was prepared, along with ten coffin bearers, all wearing newly made blue cloth long gowns. The parlor owner personally supervised them. At 7:30 AM, the ten bearers carried the coffin ashore. The parlor owner held a picture of Jesus and led the way, followed by the brothers Tzu-liang and Tzu-an, dressed in moon-white cloth robes, then Soong Mei-ling, Soong Ai-ling, and Kong Xiangxi, and finally Soong Tzu-wen, escorted by armed guards.

▲Paying Respects to the Deceased: The coffin proceeded straight along Avenue Edward VII and arrived at the Soong residence on Seymour Road at 8:00 AM.

Funeral Shed at the Soong Residence on Seymour Road (Photographed by Our Newspaper)

A funeral shed was erected in front of the house. The coffin was placed in the main hall, and a family memorial service was held. Pastor Jiang Changchuan performed a prayer, and the family surrounded the coffin in silent prayer and paid their respects to the deceased. The undertakers from the Wan Guo Funeral Parlor had previously travelled to Qingdao to perform surgery on Madam Soong's body, so her appearance was lifelike.

▲Mourners Arriving: Yesterday morning and afternoon, people from all walks of life, both Chinese and foreign, came to pay their respects in an endless stream, including Yu Qiaqing, Qian Xinzhi, Chen Xing, Guo Dehua, Guo Biao, Guo Chengen, Zheng Yuxiu, Du Yuesheng, and over three hundred others. According to the funeral director, the coffin is planned to be kept for one or two weeks before the funeral is held on a later date and buried at Hongqiao Road.

▲Customs Flies Half-Mast: Customs Superintendent Tang Haian accompanied Minister Soong to Shanghai yesterday morning and went to the Soong residence to assist with the funeral arrangements. The Jianghai Customs flew its flag at half-mast to express its condolences. The naval cruiser arrived at the Wusongkou the night before last at 10:00 PM, weighed anchor and entered the port at 5:00 AM yesterday morning, and arrived at the wharf at 7:10 AM.

Joint Defense Meeting for the Two Railways

▲Held at the Garrison Headquarters Yesterday

▲Resolution on Military-Police Cooperation Measures

The Shanghai-Songhu Garrison Headquarters convened a joint defense meeting for the two railways yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM at the Garrison Headquarters, gathering representatives from various agencies, including the Municipal Government, the Public Security Bureau, and the police forces of the two railways. Based on the instructions of the Executive Yuan, the military and police authorities jointly discussed and agreed on sound prevention measures to avoid the recurrence of unfortunate incidents. The attendees included Chief of Staff of the Garrison Headquarters Xu Jinyuan, Chief of the Staff Office Lai Weiying, Director of the Adjutant's Office Jiang Yi, Captain of the Intelligence Team Deng Jingming, Public Security Bureau Director Chen Xizeng (representing Mayor Zhang), Public Security Bureau Inspector-General Wang Yufen, Chief of the Road Bureau's Vehicle Operations Section Chen Chengshi, Chief of the Road Bureau's Police Affairs Deng Zuyu, and Adjutant of the First Regiment of the Military Police Yan Zeyuan. Xu Jinyuan was publicly elected as chairman. After formal greetings, discussions began on the jurisdiction and responsibilities of the two railways' defenses and the effective cooperation between the military and police. The meeting adjourned around 3:00 PM. This reporter interviewed the Deputy Adjutant of the Garrison Headquarters, Jiang Yi, yesterday. According to him, the joint defense meeting for the two railways resolved on measures for the military and police to distribute defense responsibilities. The military police regiment is responsible for station security, with Captain Zhang Baoguang of the military police battalion in overall command. Currently, two companies of military police are stationed near the station, and one platoon of military police is inside the station. The military police regiment is directly under the command of the Garrison Headquarters, and the Public Security Bureau and the railway police will provide full assistance. In this way, with clear responsibilities, there will be no more excuses in the event of an accident. The section of the defense area allocated by this meeting is from Nanxiang to Hangzhou. The section from Nanxiang to Nanjing is jointly managed by the Capital Garrison Headquarters, the Capital Police Department, and the Railway Department.

Further News on the Hankou Flood

▲Severe Losses to Merchants and Goods

The Yangtze River flood was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday, various shipping companies in this port continued to receive telegrams from Hankou stating that the flood situation was even worse and the disaster was more serious. The various points heard are recorded separately below:

▲River Continues to Rise: The Yangtze River water level is normally 17 to 18 feet. The shallowest point this year was 11 feet. This time, the heavy rain has not stopped, and the water level has been increasing day and night. On the 27th, it was 46 feet 6 inches, which was unprecedented. Unexpectedly, on the 28th, it rose another 3 feet. At that time, most of the roads in Hankou were flooded. Unexpectedly, that night, it rose another 2 feet, reaching a water level of 52 feet 5 inches yesterday, which is the largest flood in the Yangtze River in the past six or seventy years.

▲High Warehouses also Submerged: The Hankou telegram on the previous day stated that the water along the bank had risen to the streets, and the higher warehouses built by the various shipping companies had not yet been affected, while the rest were submerged. Various shipping companies were trying to unload the lower-level goods and move them to higher ground. Unexpectedly, the water rose sharply that day, and by the night of the 28th, the higher warehouses were also completely flooded, and more goods were damaged by the water. In addition, traffic was obstructed due to the flooding of various roads, making rescue efforts difficult to implement.

▲Goods Blocked Upstream: The goods coming to Hankou on the Yangtze River are all from upstream ports, such as Shashi, Yichang, and Changsha, Xiangtan, and the goods from various ports on the Pinghan Railway are transferred to Shanghai. Since the 27th, the joint transportation of goods on the Pinghan Railway has been blocked by the flood, and no goods have been loaded. Goods from Shashi, Yichang, and other places have also been blocked because they cannot be unloaded. Therefore, the downstream goods of various Yangtze River ships have suddenly decreased.

▲Grain Transported to Hankou: The food supply in Hankou has been affected by the flood. Recently, the Hankou merchants have sent telegrams to Shanghai one after another to purchase food and transport it to Hankou to provide relief to the people. A large amount of foreign rice and wheat flour has been purchased in Shanghai in recent days. Yesterday, the Dehe De Lun ship loaded 7,477 bags of white rice, and the Datong Lun and Wuchang Lun ships transported another 2,411 bags. A considerable amount of wheat flour was also loaded and transported.

Mayor Zhang's Talk

▲Splitting Business Tax with Jiangsu Provincial Government

▲Second Batch of Land in the Central District to be Released

▲Hopes Anti-Japanese Association Will Strictly Observe Discipline

A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency visited Mayor Zhang Qun yesterday regarding the Jiangsu Provincial Government's request to the Executive Yuan to allocate the revenue from the business tax of the two municipal governments of Nanjing and Shanghai, with the province receiving 70% and the city receiving 30%, and the issue of land in the central district. He asked for his opinions as follows:

▲Assisting with Business Tax: Mayor Zhang said that after the Municipal Government of Shanghai received the order from the Executive Yuan to consider the issue of the business tax assisting the Jiangsu Provincial Government, it had already reported the difficult-to-assist situation to the Executive Yuan based on reason. There are three reasons why it cannot assist: First, administratively, the Shanghai Municipal Government is an independent municipal agency, different from others that are subordinate to the provincial government. All municipal construction depends on the revenue of the city, and the development of the entire city depends on it. Therefore, in reality, there is no surplus capacity to assist. Second, Shanghai has a special relationship with the concessions. The taxes and levies that all other provinces and cities have are unique to Shanghai and cannot be implemented. For example, in the past, the Municipal Government planned to levy a wine and banquet tax, but it could not be realized due to the restrictions of the concessions. At present, what the municipal treasury relies on to supplement is still the old tax revenue from the past, which has been rectified. Although it seems to have increased slightly compared to before, all future construction and development of the Municipal Government require funds. Therefore, it is considered that the only hope is the income from the municipal business tax. The amount of income from the municipal business tax, however, is not only impossible to determine before collection, but also impossible to estimate. Moreover, the tax rate in Shanghai is lower compared to other provinces, with the highest being only 3 per thousand. In the future, when collecting taxes, although Chinese merchants in the concessions will all recognize paying taxes as a due obligation and enthusiastically agree, the Municipal Government must also consider their burdens. Chinese merchants in the concessions cannot be exempt from paying all miscellaneous taxes in the concessions just because they have already paid the business tax to the Municipal Government. For example, recently, the hotel industry in the concessions has requested to use capital as the basis for tax collection, and the Municipal Government cannot but consider it. In the future, foreign merchants in the concessions will naturally also be included in the collection. However, foreign merchants also have the obligation to fulfill their corresponding obligations to their home government. Under these circumstances, the Municipal Government seems to need to be considerate. Therefore, the income from the municipal business tax in the future is still difficult to predict due to various special circumstances. Third, what is taken from the people should be used for the people. I still remember that when preparing for the business tax, someone said that Shanghai would collect the business tax in the future, and the Chinese area would naturally not have much problem, but the taxpayers in the concessions only have the obligation to pay taxes and have no rights to benefit. If the concessions collect the business tax, the Municipal Government should pay attention to the interests of the taxpayers in the concessions. His words are very reasonable, but the Municipal Government has never excluded the citizens of the concessions from the benefits of the citizens. For example, education and sanitation are provided to the citizens of both the Chinese and concession areas with equal benefits. Therefore, in the future, the Municipal Government will still use the revenue from the business tax for the people, adding schools and sanitation facilities to seek happiness for the citizens. The Greater Shanghai Plan and other plans all rely on this income. Therefore, the request of the provincial government is in fact impossible.

▲Continued Opening of Land: This time, the land reclamation in the central district involved more than 800 mu. Careful consideration was given beforehand to ensure comprehensiveness and meticulousness. However, it was unexpected that citizens would reclaim land so enthusiastically. This is indeed a good phenomenon of citizens' faith in the government. At the same time, the worry that no one would register to reclaim land has been easily replaced by an unusually joyful feeling. In the original plan of the Municipal Government, registration would come first, followed by lottery, and those who drew first would reclaim first, to avoid disputes. Unexpectedly, on that day, the Land Bureau reported that those who were reclaiming land were rushing to be first, and someone temporarily called others to the Land Bureau to help draw lots. Therefore, I temporarily decided to set the standard of reclaiming a certain amount of land with a certain amount of funds. Therefore, some people were inevitably disappointed. As for the land reclaimed by the Shanghai Bank, it was also a combination of multiple people drawing lots, and there was no other relationship. After this issue occurred, I once summoned the Shanghai Bank for questioning. It is indeed not a trust. The outside world's rumors are actually a misunderstanding. At present, the Municipal Government plans to use the land reclamation funds immediately for the construction of trunk roads and ditches in the central district. At the same time, 540 mu in the northwest of the central district will be reopened. The reclamation method will be reversed from the previous regulations. First, each person will only reclaim one mu, then each person will reclaim two mu, then three mu, and then four mu. This will definitely avoid the disadvantages of incompleteness.

▲Attitude Towards Anti-Japanese: He then talked about the citizens' Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Overseas-Chinese Association implementing the detention of goods, saying briefly that he deeply sympathized with the citizens' patriotic enthusiasm, but hoped that all actions could be within the scope of the law, not exceeding the boundaries of the track, and could use the personality of self-respect and respect for others to carry out a disciplined and orderly movement.

Change of Bureau Directors on Two Routes ▲Guo Cheng'en Succeeds

Luo Panhui, the Director of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, who had only assumed office four months ago, suddenly received an order from the Ministry of Railways yesterday, transferring him to the Ministry for assignment. Measures for Inspecting Weights and Measures in the Concession

▲Already Agreed Upon Through Negotiation by the Authorities

The inspection of weights and measures in this city is divided into four phases: the first phase is the Hunan District, the second phase is the Zhabei District, the third phase is the Concession District, and the fourth phase is the Four Townships District. Inspections have already been implemented. Regarding the inspection issue in the Public Concession, Yu Hongjun, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, and Feixin Dun, the Director-General of the Municipal Council, have negotiated and generally agreed. As for the inspection procedures, a consultation was held at the Municipal Government's After-Hours Club on Weihaiwei Road at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday (the 28th). Those present included Yu Hongjun, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, Pan Gongzhan, the Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, Wu Hengru, the Section Chief, Zhou Zanming, the Director of the Weights and Measures Verification Institute, Feixin Dun, the Director-General of the Municipal Council, and Mao Ding, the Chief Inspector. The results of the consultation are as follows: (1) Regarding the inspection of weights and measures in the Special District, the Social Affairs Bureau will order the Weights and Measures Verification Institute to designate five inspectors to handle it. (2) Inspectors must carry an execution inspection certificate with their photo attached and stamped with the seal of the Weights and Measures Verification Institute. The Social Affairs Bureau will send the format of the inspection certificate to the Municipal Council in advance for distribution to each police station for record-keeping. (3) If police stations encounter inspectors holding inspection certificates requesting assistance with inspection, they should immediately dispatch police to assist. (4) Matters regarding penalties for violations of laws and regulations will be transferred to the Special District Local Court for handling. It is said that the initial inspection will adopt a method of persuasion, setting a time limit for compliance with the new instruments.

Bloodshed on Killarney Road

▲Zhou Chunsheng Dies Tragically from Gunshot

▲Seemingly a Homicide Due to Adultery

At around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, Zhou Chunsheng, a native of Suzhou residing in the rear building of No. 32 Guangyu Lane on Killarney Road in the French Concession, was suddenly assassinated and killed by thugs with a gunshot. His concubine, Hu Zhou, was also seriously injured at the same time. The details are recorded as follows:

▲Subletting Spare Rooms Qiao Hanzhou, a 37-year-old Suzhou native, is engaged in the tailoring business. He married Guo, who is currently 34 years old. Qiao is naturally frugal and has some savings. Eight years ago, he rented No. 32 Guangyu Lane on Killarney Road in the French Concession and became a sublandlord. In addition to opening his own Qiao Hanji Tailoring Shop in the front downstairs room, all the remaining rooms upstairs were sublet to others.

▲Operating a "Swallows' Nest" Qiao rented the front building to a newspaper vendor named Chen Jinbao and the attic to a Mr. Shi. The remaining rear building was only rented to Zhou Chunsheng (No. 31), a native of Hengjing, Suzhou, on the 14th of this month. The rent was set at seven and a half yuan per month. Zhou had a concubine, Hu Zhou (27 years old, from the same hometown as Zhou), who moved in with him. When renting the room, Zhou claimed to the sublandlord that he intended to temporarily open a "swallows' nest" before renting a small house to live in.

▲Three Shots Fired Zhou and his concubine moved in, Zhou left early and returned late every day, while Hu Zhou stayed at home all day without taking a step beyond the threshold. At around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, Zhou and his concubine were still fast asleep, neck and neck in bed. The downstairs shop door had just opened, and the apprentice was sweeping when suddenly a thug wearing a dark blue Xiangyun gauze short jacket and trousers and a straw hat broke in, rushed upstairs, and burst open the rear building door. Upon seeing Zhou and Hu Zhou still sound asleep, he took out a pistol and fired three shots at the bed.

▲Unsuccessful Pursuit of the Murderer At the sound of the gunfire, one bullet hit Zhou's left temple, and another hit Hu Zhou's right breast. Hu Zhou was awakened by the injury and witnessed the murderer fleeing downstairs in a panic. Hu Zhou hurriedly chased downstairs with her wound. At the same time, the sublandlord was startled awake and ran barefoot out the door, intending to help with the pursuit. However, the murderer turned back and threatened Qiao with a gun. Qiao became timid and dared not pursue further. The murderer then calmly left the alley and fled south towards Tangjiawan without a trace.

▲Husband Dead, Wife Wounded Qiao turned back and saw blood streaming from Hu Zhou's chest. He immediately hired a car to report to the Songshan Road Police Station. The police chief ordered Hu Zhou to be sent to Renji Hospital for treatment and dispatched detectives to the scene of the incident for investigation. Zhou Chunsheng had already died due to the fatal wound. His body was then transported to the Tongren Fuyuan sub-hall morgue for examination. It was discovered that the deceased had no family members in Shanghai. Subsequently, the Criminal Division of the French General Police Department reported to the French Concession Court Judge Zhu Chengshen, who arrived at the morgue at 2:00 PM to confirm that Zhou Chunsheng had been assassinated. The detective then reported the previous events. After the judge questioned the sublandlord, he ordered the body to be photographed and taken into custody by the morgue pending the police's arrest and investigation of the murderer.

▲The Concubine's Account According to Hu Zhou, she and the deceased, Chunsheng, had previously opened a "swallows' nest" in the front building of No. 107 Annakin Road in the French Concession and were planning to move to Guangyu Lane to continue the business. Unexpectedly, this accident occurred. She had only known the deceased for a short time. As for the murderer, he resembled a familiar fellow villager named Chen Caifa. The reporter's investigation revealed that the case was mostly caused by adultery, resulting in a murder due to jealousy.

Disruption of Yangtze Ferry Operation

▲Delaying More Than Two Thousand People's Work for One Hour

▲Shipping Bureau Agrees to Investigate and Negotiate Compensation

At around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, water police officers stopped the Yangtze ferry from crossing the river, causing a disturbance among more than two thousand male and female workers gathered on the shore. Fortunately, the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team learned of this and immediately dispatched police to the scene to quell the situation. The details are recorded as follows: The Yangtze ferry started operating at the Qichangzhan Wharf. After the construction was completed, it shuttled back and forth across the river, transporting workers to and from factories, carrying approximately thousands of people each day.

At around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, when the ferry was docked near the Qichangzhan Wharf in Pudong, fully loaded with workers on the wharf built along the riverbank, it was preparing to set sail to Puxi. At that time, Water Police Officer No. 78 suddenly arrived, claiming that the number of passengers on board exceeded the quota and prohibiting it from crossing the river. The ferry then checked and found only forty-two passengers, arguing that it did not exceed the prescribed limit and still requesting permission to sail. However, the police officer insisted on refusing, causing a delay of about one hour. Consequently, workers had gradually gathered on the shore, numbering over two thousand. Because they could not cross the river, they were late for work. They all believed that the police officer had unreasonably prevented the ferry from sailing, and the crowd became angry, causing a disturbance. Dozens of female workers, in particular, felt indignant and swarmed forward, dragging the police officer to the Gonghexiang Wharf and berating him. Seeing this situation, the ferry was deeply afraid of causing a major disaster and immediately sounded a distress call, emitting several loud wails. Nearby boatmen, unaware of the truth, became panicked. This was heard by Liu, an officer of the Lujiazui Police Station of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team, who immediately dispatched several senior police officers to rush to the scene to quell the situation, which was then calmed down. By this time, the Water Police Station had also learned of the incident and immediately dispatched personnel to the scene to comfort the workers. Police Officer No. 78, knowing that he could not withstand the public's anger, took the opportunity to sit alone in a sampan and rushed back to the Yangshupu Sub-station of the Water Police. At this time, more than two thousand workers, because the time for entering the factory had passed, could not enter the factory to work. The loss of one day's wages was substantial. They demanded that the ferry transport all the workers to the Water Police Station for negotiations. The entire crew of the ferry, fearing further incidents, after earnestly persuading the crowd, jointly traveled to the Jianghaiguan Shipping Bureau with two patrol boats of the Water Police, where the workers demanded that the bureau quickly seek compensation from the Water Police for the losses incurred due to the unreasonable delay in going to work. At that time, both sides deliberated repeatedly, but there was still no result. Finally, the bureau agreed to wait for an investigation of the cause of the incident before further processing. The workers were then gradually transported back by the ferry, and the disturbance temporarily came to an end. The ferry owner, Chen Songtao, and others, after the incident, presented a request to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team, stating that the Shanghai Water Police's unreasonable obstruction of navigation, obstruction of traffic, and delay of workers' time to work had aroused public anger and almost caused a major disaster, and that such behavior would have a significant impact on future business operations. Therefore, they requested that the Bureau find ways to protect them in order to prevent future troubles.

Huang Chujiu's Assets to Be Auctioned by Public Advertisement

▲Based on the Highest Bid

▲Huang's Assets Awaiting Investigation

The case of the Shanghai Riyue Bank and the Great World Amusement Savings Department going bankrupt was heard again by the French Concession Court yesterday afternoon. First, accountant Pan Zhaobang reported on the change from bidding to liquidation, stating that Huang's family, after being ordered to clear the assets by the accountants, submitted a public list through Huang's family's lawyer, Tan Yigong, stating that Huang's real estate and movable property totaled several million, and even movable property alone was worth hundreds of thousands. Unexpectedly, when the goods were delivered, all the pearls were found to be extremely small and yellow, and the utensils and other items were worth no more than several hundred yuan in total, which was vastly different from the amount reported by lawyer Tan. He requested verification. Tan Yigong, the lawyer representing Huang's family, requested that the previous court order for bidding be cancelled. Yu Chengxiu, the deputy lawyer representing the creditors' rights and obligations lawyer Wu Jingxiong, stated that the case had been in litigation for a long time, and the creditors had only received 10% of their rights. After the previous court order changed the bidding to liquidation, various disputes arose, with articles competing to be published in newspapers, with thousands of words. The creditor side was very distressed by this kind of pointless dispute. Huang Chujiu was both a director and manager of the Gongfa Company, occupying the position of a natural debtor. After the previous court order for liquidation, his representative lawyer Tan Yigong publicly submitted a property list report stating that Huang had total assets of more than six million, which made all creditors very happy. Unexpectedly, according to the accountant's report, the assets were only worth more than 1.7 million, a difference of four to five million, and even this 1.7 million was not a real figure. Upon hearing this, all the creditors felt as if cold water had been poured on them, which was very disappointing and caused dissatisfaction. The previous court order to change the bidding to liquidation was supported by all creditor representatives, who still requested public advertisement for bidding in order to close the case as soon as possible. Lawyer Jiang Yiping also stated that the winning bidders from the previous bidding were now suing the accountant in the Special District Court, requesting a public letter from the court to prove that the two biddings were actually abolished by the court's decision, to avoid the accountant being implicated due to public affairs. Lawyer Zhu Shuzhen also stated that he also represented some of the creditors, and that now there were rumors among thousands of people outside that Huang's family had only handed over a portion of the property after receiving the court order for liquidation, and that a large portion of the property was hidden and not handed over. According to the accountant's report, only a few hundred yuan worth of jewelry was handed over in terms of movable property. Huang Chujiu could be called a wealthy man, so how could he only have this meager jewelry? He requested the court to order Huang's family to hand over the majority of the property. Lawyer Yan Luqing also stated that Huang's family still had a large number of diamonds and other items that had been mortgaged to others. He requested the court to summon the case for questioning. There was also the matter of the Wanchun Silver Group contract, which was somewhat unclear and should also be investigated in order to close the case as soon as possible. After the lawyers debated for a long time, Judge Gong issued an order stating that the request from Huang's family to revoke the court order of July 18 was opposed by all the creditor representatives, and that the previous court order to abolish the two biddings should still be followed. The accountant was allowed to join with the various representative lawyers to advertise for public bidding, with the highest bid as the standard. Some creditor representative lawyers also stated that the accountant should investigate and report the situation of Huang's family concealing property.

Legal Opinion on Tan Yigong Lawyer's Clearing of Huang Chujiu's Assets (Continued)

(4) Legal Points Regarding the Handling of Huang's Debts: The debts left by Huang Chujiu refer to private debts (such as Huang Chujiu's household in Riyue Bank with more than one million, and other mortgage and borrowing debts of nearly two million) and debts incurred from business operations (such as the share to be borne when the partnership property of Gongfa Company is insufficient to pay debts, and debts from other sole proprietorships or partnerships). Huang Chujiu's private debts to others are even greater than the debts owed to Great World and Riyue Bank, etc. under Gongfa Company. Whether or not the debts are recognized, waived, or reduced is not something that the liquidator of Gongfa Company can handle. Using Huang's entire property to repay Huang's entire debt is even more inappropriate to entrust to the liquidator of Gongfa Company, who represents only part of the creditors, to dispose of and distribute the entire property alone. Because Huang's entire estate has been determined by the court to repay all the debts he owed privately and from operating businesses, the total amount of money obtained from selling the property should be paid off separately to those with priority rights, liens, and mortgage rights according to the total amount of all debts, and then distributed equally to ordinary creditors. The debts owed by Huang Chujiu's household in Riyue Bank and Great World are one of the ordinary debts, and should be paid off equally with other ordinary creditors, without any superior rights, which is very obvious.

(5) Legal Points Regarding the Interference of Gongfa Company's Creditor's Representative Lawyer in the Disposal of Huang Chujiu's Estate: Huang Chujiu has two positions in Gongfa Company: one is as a shareholder, and the other is as a debtor of the Riyue Bank Great World under the company. Regarding the shareholder status, he should be in the same position as other general shareholders. Before Gongfa Company is completely closed and it has not been proven that all the partnership property is insufficient to pay off debts, he is not responsible for any liabilities. As for the debtor status, the creditor of his business is Gongfa Company, not the creditors of Gongfa Company. Therefore, the creditors of Gongfa Company and their representative lawyers have no direct creditor-debtor relationship with Huang's estate, and naturally have no right to participate in and interfere with Huang's estate. Moreover, the liquidation affairs of Gongfa Company have long been assigned by Junxie to accountants Pan and Wu as liquidators to represent their rights. If the creditor representative lawyer has any opinions and claims, they can contribute and request Pan and Wu. If they believe that Pan and Wu are not sufficient to protect the rights of the Gongfa Company's creditors, they can also request Junxie to provide legal relief. Moreover, clearing Huang's estate and clearing Gongfa Company are two completely different matters. The creditor representative lawyer of Gongfa Company cannot interfere with the clearing of Huang's estate, just as Huang's private creditors can only claim against Huang's family and Huang's representative lawyer, and cannot interfere with the clearing of Gongfa Company. Putting it another way, it is very clear. However, the creditor representative lawyers Dong Yu, Dong Chi, Chen Zhigao, Jiang Yiping, etc., either interfered with the bidding process, causing disputes, or criticized the bidding methods approved by Junxie, requesting changes, and even said that Huang's estate had already been handed over and that Huang's family and Huang's representatives should not interfere. The biggest mistake is that they regard Huang Chujiu as Gongfa Company, and regard Huang Chujiu's estate as Gongfa Company's property. Whether the lawyers have other opinions, I dare not comment, but it can be asserted that the lawyers have no legal grounds to interfere with the clearing of Huang's estate.

(6) Legal Points Regarding Wu and Pan Accountants Being Appointed as Liquidators of Gongfa Company, Simultaneously Representing the Court to Take Care of Huang's Estate, and Being Ordered to Handle Huang's Estate Together with Huang's Family Representatives: According to the order of Junxie, accountants Pan and Wu are the liquidators of Gongfa Company. With this qualification alone, they have no right to interfere with Huang's estate. The reason they can participate in clearing Huang's estate is that they were also appointed as custodians of Huang's estate and were ordered by Junxie on March 30 to discuss solutions together, standing in the position of supervising and assisting Huang's clearing. Since the accountant has several qualifications as a natural person, the general creditors of Gongfa Company mistakenly believe that the accountant can use the qualification of the liquidator of Gongfa Company to dispose of Huang's estate, resulting in unnecessary disputes. Gongfa Company and Huang are in a position of relative creditor-debtor relationship, and the liquidator of Gongfa Company should focus on the interests of Gongfa Company as their task. Since the interests are biased, it will inevitably have an adverse impact on Huang's family and his private creditors. The fact that the accountants announced the bidding in the name of the liquidator of Gongfa Company, and did not discuss solutions together with Huang's representative, but reported to the court and published the advertisement alone to negotiate the sale of Huang's estate, and never mentioned Huang's private debts from beginning to end, is sufficient to prove this. In order to avoid misunderstandings and show impartiality, Junxie should revoke one or two of the accountant's qualifications and appoint another person to take over in order to clarify the boundaries and quell disputes.

(7) Points Regarding the Methods of Handling Huang's Estate and Distributing Debts: Since Huang's entire estate has been approved to pay off all debts, for the sake of Huang's family and Huang's creditors, it should be closed as soon as possible. Based on the current situation, solutions are proposed separately as follows: (1) Real estate: (a) The first batch of real estate bid out includes a total of six properties. Except for the ownership of the Fang Dan property, which is still under investigation, and the Xicang Road property, which has been reviewed and decided to be re-bid, the remaining three properties, the Jiu Fu Company on Baike Road, the Xinghua Restaurant on Simalu, and the Yi Jia property, are more significant. The bid prices obtained are not far apart. Since they have been reviewed and determined and the winning bidders have been notified according to law, in order to maintain the court's authority, it seems appropriate to allow the bidder with the highest bid amount to win the bid in order to stop litigation and avoid complications. (b) For those whose first and second bids have not been reviewed and determined, Huang's liquidator should be allowed to advertise the highest bid publicly for purchase, and the reserve price must be above the highest original bid price. If a reasonable price is still not obtained for the first time, the advertisement should be published for the second time, and the reserve price must be above the previous highest bid, with the highest bidder as the winner. This public bidding can increase the value, so that creditors can benefit more and show fairness to dispel outside rumors. When publishing the bidding advertisement, the contract relationship and advantages of each real estate should be attached in detail to attract buyers' attention. All methods for implementing the bidding should be subject to the approval of the supervisors. (2) Disposal of movable property: Since a portion has been sold by the liquidator of Gongfa Company, the remaining portion should still be handled in the same way by the liquidator, selling it by auction with a reserve price. The amount of the reserve price must first be approved by Huang's liquidator. (3) Disposal of most of the sole proprietorship stores: Since a portion was previously sold by the liquidator of Gongfa Company, the remaining portion should still be handled in the same way. (4) Method of collecting, paying, and storing money: Since all the estate is sold in succession, the money from the sale should be jointly issued a receipt by the supervisor and Huang's representative, stored in the banks designated by Junxie, the checks should be kept by Huang's liquidator with two seals for withdrawing money, one held by the supervisor designated by Junxie and the other held by Huang's liquidator. Both parties must seal together before payment can be made. At the end of each month, a detailed statement of receipts and payments should be prepared, reported, and published in the newspaper to reduce the responsibility of all parties. Since the amount of money coming in and out is very large, it is not enough to value social credit without mutual strict responsibility. (5) Method of distribution: After all the estate has been sold and priced, the total amount of Huang Chujiu's private debts and debts from operating businesses should be repaid separately to those with priority rights, mortgage rights, and liens, and the remaining ordinary debts should be distributed equally, assisted by the supervisor and Huang's liquidator. (6) Method of closing: After all the estate is sold and priced and distributed to the various debts, the supervisor appointed by the court and Huang's liquidator should each submit a final report to the various courts for record and announce the closure of Huang's liquidation. The report should also be sent to all relevant parties for their information. The remaining items with no value that cannot be sold (such as Gongfa Company stocks) should still be returned to Huang's family for storage. In summary, as this lawyer's duty, I dare not remain silent and specially list my views, requesting Junxie to review and approve them as soon as possible, which would be in the public interest.

Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai French Concession Mixed Court for your consideration.

▲Great World Sale Price... Distribute Promptly

Zhang Shiming's Deceased Concubine Appeals Again on the Issue of Mother-Son Relationship

▲Zhang Qu'an Must Appear in Court

▲Zhou Miaoying Will Not Make Things Difficult

Zhou Miaoying, the former concubine of the deceased wealthy Nanzun businessman Zhang Shiming, filed a lawsuit through lawyers Yuan Yang'an, Zhang Zirang, and others to confirm her mother-son relationship with her son, Qu'an, because she was not consulted when he got engaged and married. The defendants, Zhang Qu'an and Zhang Xu Shi (Zhang Shiming's legal wife), also hired three lawyers, Zhu Sisti, Jiang Yiping, and Cai Ni Pei, to defend them, claiming that Zhou had already received 40,000 yuan and severed her family ties. As for Zhang Qu'an, they acknowledged Zhou Miaoying as his biological mother. As a result, Zhou Miaoying lost the case. Zhou appealed to the High Court, and the court had summoned them once before. Moreover, the lawyer argued that since the appellant had received 40,000 yuan and had lost her status, she could not file another claim. Judge Hu immediately stated that since the appellee had already acknowledged the plaintiff as his biological mother, why was there a need for her to appear in court again? Lawyer Zhang replied that it was for the convenience of reconciliation. Judge Li also declared that since the appellee had already acknowledged the appellant as his mother, why was she filing a lawsuit to confirm their mother-son relationship? If she wanted to assert her rights, that was a different issue and not within the scope of this case. The judge added that it would not hurt for the appellee to appear in court once and that it would be better to have him confront her at the next hearing. Lawyer Zhu Sisti then stated that Zhang Qu'an was not unwilling to appear in court, but he was afraid that the appellant would intercept him and cause a disturbance in or outside the courtroom, so he dared not appear. If the appellant did not engage in such behavior, he would definitely appear next time. Lawyer Zhang stated that they would definitely not make things difficult for the appellee. Judge Hu then adjourned the hearing and announced that they would wait for Zhang Qu'an to be summoned to court for verification.

A Madwoman's Utterances

▲Having a Major Nervous Breakdown and Making Trouble Everywhere

▲Rumored to Have Run a Brothel, Depleted Her Wealth, and Turned Eccentric

At around 1:00 AM yesterday morning, a barefoot madwoman, approximately in her twenties, wearing a bean-paste-colored wool georgette cheongsam, a white cambric shirt and pants with frills, and a black satin gauze vest, suddenly appeared in Renmei Lane, West Xinjiao Street, French Concession. A young man, claiming to be her husband, followed behind. They walked to the street-crossing building at No. 1 in the lane and sat down on the ground. The man tried to persuade her to leave the alley, but the woman had a major nervous breakdown, spouting nonsense. She began taking off her clothes one by one, even attempting to remove her undershirt and pants. The man forcibly stopped her, and she began rolling around on the ground, covering herself in mud and filth, making a stinking mess. She kept arguing and making noise all night, grabbing onto passersby and food vendors, preventing the residents of the entire lane from sleeping. After dawn, when the garbage trucks entered the lane, residents opened their doors to empty their chamber pots. The madwoman saw the back door of No. 1 Zhizhong Lane wide open (this back door opened into Renmei Lane) and rushed in, bolting the door shut and sneaking into the bedroom. The cleaning lady of the house saw her and was shocked. The man outside the door, unable to enter because the back door was bolted, explained the situation and forced the door open. After great effort, he managed to carry the madwoman out, but she immediately lay down on the ground again. Moments later, she sneaked into the back door of No. 2 Renmei Lane, climbed up to the attic, closed it tightly, and lay down on the floor. The man tried to enter and drag her out, but the door was locked and he could not get in. He borrowed a ladder from a neighbor, climbed in through the window, and with great effort, dragged the madwoman out. In a short time, a large crowd gathered in the lane. Onlookers advised the man to hire a car and take her to a hospital for treatment. Afterwards, someone familiar with the madwoman said that she was 27 years old, from Wuxi, and had previously run a brothel in the French Concession, with three "persons to ask for" (i.e., girls). She had accumulated some savings but had spent it all on a man (the one who accompanied her to the hospital). Both of them were addicted to opium, and now they had run out of money and the prostitutes had also escaped one after another. This had caused her to suffer a mental breakdown.

Warning Signs Erected on the Wusong Seaside

▲Advising People Not to Drown Themselves

The Wusong Municipal Committee Office, recognizing that many aimless young people often come to Wusong to commit suicide by drowning, and that the causes are nothing more than economic oppression and heartbreak, which lead to meaningless sacrifices in the vast ocean among countless living beings, decided to find a way to help. They produced ten warning signs and erected them along the coast so that those contemplating suicide would see them and be awakened, turning back as soon as possible. Yesterday, they sent staff to survey the locations and erect the signs, from Yunzaobang Bridge to Fort Taiwan. The slogans used were all contributed by various organizations. Here are some excerpts: "Only by living and struggling can you solve your problems!" "Failure is the mother of success; suicide is the act of the weak." "Why care so much for a heartless person? Heartbreak is your happiness; why do you need to die?" "You die for him/her, and he/she laughs at your foolishness. You must not die; see how foolish he/she is!" "Don't get it wrong; it's easy to seek death, but hard to seek life. Turn back quickly!"
