The Current Status of the Trust Department of the Continental Bank

▲Manager Shen's Remarks

Since the Continental Bank established its Shanghai Trust Department in December of last year, engaging in various trust businesses, it has achieved remarkable results in the past six months. The end of June this year marked the end of the first half of the year for accounting purposes. All fixed-term trust deposits with a term of two years or more were allocated a dividend of 3.5%, which, together with the guaranteed interest, resulted in an annual interest rate of at least 1.15% and at most 1.45%. This high level of profit is unmatched by ordinary bank fixed-term deposits. Mr. Shen Erchang, director of the bank and manager of the Shanghai Trust Department, discussed the fundamental differences between trust deposits and ordinary bank fixed-term deposits as follows: The trust business originated in England and flourished in the United States. The English system focuses on managing property for others, while the American system focuses on utilizing funds for others. Both manage property for others at the same time. The German system falls between the English and American systems, and the Japanese system follows the German model. In our country, the trust business is just beginning to emerge, and there are no trust laws yet. Our bank, which also handles trust business, has been approved by the ministry and operates carefully based on precedents from various countries and taking into account our country's circumstances. Trust matters are fundamentally different from banking matters. A bank's profits mainly come from interest, remittance fees, and exchange rates, with other types of income being minimal. Legal restrictions prevent banks from directly engaging in industry and commerce, so the profits are derived solely from providing capital to industry and commerce and collecting interest. Therefore, the level of bank interest rates is closely related to industry and commerce. To promote the prosperity of industry and commerce, bank lending rates should not be too high, and deposit rates are naturally subject to related restrictions. Banking associations in various countries often have agreements on interest rates. Trust business is generally divided into managing property for others and utilizing funds for others. The former is completely different from banking business, while the latter is similar to but fundamentally different from bank fixed-term deposits. Although the methods of utilizing funds in the trust business vary from country to country, direct investment is openly permitted. Japanese trust law stipulates the buying and selling of movable and immovable property, with more than twenty types of movable property specified by the Ministry of Finance, including all the goods needed for social life. Therefore, the profits from utilizing funds in the trust business include both capital interest and enterprise profits. The guaranteed interest on trust deposits is the interest due on capital, and the dividends on trust deposits are the profits earned by the enterprise. Therefore, the position of a trust depositor is equivalent to making a direct investment and receiving both types of profits. The trust department distributes all profits to the depositors after deducting expenses according to regulations. This is the fundamental difference between trust deposits and ordinary bank fixed-term deposits. One cannot compare the benefits of trust deposits with bank deposits by comparing the eye of bank deposit. The original interest rate set by the department for trust deposits was 7% guaranteed interest for a two-year term, with an additional 0.5% per year for each year beyond two years, up to 1.1% guaranteed interest for a ten-year term. Accounts are settled every six months, with the same dividend distributed regardless of the length of the term, and paid out once a year after the annual settlement or compounded in advance with compound interest. The department is still in the process of expanding the profit rate of enterprises to meet the expectations of the trustees. According to the original interest rate set by the department, there is a difference of 4% between the minimum and maximum guaranteed interest rates. Although the terms are divided into two and ten years, the general opinion of depositors is that the guaranteed interest on trust deposits seems slightly lower at 7% for a two-year term and too high at over 1.1% for a ten-year term when compared to the interest on bank fixed-term deposits. It is hoped that the department will make some corrections, so that if the department's business gradually develops in the future, the dividend may be higher than 3.5%, which will not reduce the long-term income, while slightly increasing the short-term income, avoiding the difference of 4% between the highest and lowest interest rates. The department should consider the above opinions and may make slight changes to the highest guaranteed interest rate from the beginning of 1932, while not reducing the lowest guaranteed interest rate. In Japanese trust companies, interest on trust deposits is paid every six months. The department considers a six-month term too short for sufficient flexibility in utilizing funds, which may lead to imbalance. However, the method of paying both principal and interest together upon maturity, common for bank fixed-term deposits, is not suitable for those who need a fixed income every year. Therefore, the department has considered the two and decided to settle accounts annually at the end of the year and pay out the guaranteed interest and dividends together. Those who need it can budget for their annual income, and those who do not can accumulate compound interest year by year, with the aim of maximizing the benefits for the depositors and increasing the department's responsibility for social service.

Ill-Fated Lovers

▲Due to Economic Pressure

▲Husband and Wife Commit Suicide by Poisoning

Cai Aisheng, a local resident living at No. 148 Kang Nai Tuo Road, was found dead by his mother, Ms. Xu, at around 11:00 AM yesterday morning. Ms. Xu entered Aisheng's room to wake him up, only to find her son and daughter-in-law, Ms. Shen, lying side-by-side, unresponsive, and with pale faces as if they had been severely poisoned. She immediately reported to the Ge Deng Road Police Station, and the Xinzha Fire Brigade ambulance transported the two to Bao Long Hospital. However, they were already dead upon arrival. At around 3:00 PM, the bodies were transferred to the Fei Lun Road morgue for an autopsy. The deceased, Cai Aisheng, was 26 years old and previously worked in the bamboo industry but was currently unemployed. His wife, Ms. Shen, was only 19 years old. It is said that their suicide was due to economic pressure. After Aisheng lost his job, he struggled to make ends meet and had to borrow money to survive, leading to a mounting debt that he could not repay. He resorted to this extreme measure and committed suicide by poisoning.

A Scene from a Sibling Lawsuit

▲Born of the Same Root

▲Why Must You Torment Each Other So Harshly?

The late construction contractor Yu Jintang had a son named Yu Zhenmin, also known as De Bao. In that year, he acquired a house in Zhabei, Jinling Road, and named the lane after De Bao. He also had a daughter named Yu Zhenhua, who was ten years older than Zhenmin. In 1927, Jintang passed away. At that time, Zhenmin was young, and all the family affairs were managed by Zhenhua. Relying on her control of the family fortune, she became addicted to gambling. Last year, Zhenhua married a dentist, Mr. Li, and Zhenmin was also about to get married. Before the wedding, Zhenhua drew up a property division agreement, dividing her father's house in the Chunyin Lane on Ge Deng Road and the house in De Bao Lane in half. Although her husband was not a live-in son-in-law, she invited Mr. Li to live with them. Zhenmin could not bear this, so he sued her in the Special District Court to reduce the payment, determine the payment schedule and account details, and allow him and his wife to move out. The court has summoned her several times. Zhenhua, unaware that she was adopted by the Song family, falsely claimed that her brother was not a Yu. She also refused to pay the monthly average rent of 379 yuan from the two houses on Ge Deng Road and Jinling Road, only giving her brother 2.4 yuan last month and nothing this month. Yesterday, she was summoned to court again. The plaintiff's lawyer requested in court that the property division agreement be revoked. The manager of the Wufengzhuang Bank presented the account books, proving that on December 1, 1930, a bill of exchange numbered 26787 from Dingkangzhuang, worth 9,000 yuan, was personally deposited by Li Yu (i.e., Zhenhua) into Wufengzhuang the next day, secretly changing the account name to Song Yueji.

The Founding of the Foci Pharmaceutical Factory

Chinese medicine is based on five thousand years of practical experience and is a great synthesis. Therefore, its great effectiveness and proven usefulness are sufficient to serve as the foundation for twentieth-century scientific medicine. If the Chinese medicines obtained from ancient experience can be reformed to remove the outdated and unrealistic theories since the Jin and Yuan dynasties, and improved and elucidated based on the latest scientific medical principles and using physicochemical pharmaceutical methods, they will surely be welcomed by the global medical community. The international academic status can also improve steadily. In 1921, Mr. Li Pingshu, Yu Botao, Wang Zude, and Zheng Pingshu, recognizing this, took the improvement of Chinese medicine as their responsibility and founded the Cuihua Pharmaceutical Factory in Shanghai. After three years of hard work and sacrificing hundreds of thousands of dollars, they had to stop due to circumstances and aspirations. Mr. Zheng Pingshu, with a spirit of perseverance, poured all his personal wealth into starting the Guohua Pharmaceutical Factory, hoping to continue the unfinished business, but it also stalled due to unfavorable circumstances.

In the spring of 1929, several lay Buddhists under the contemporary eminent monk Master Taixu, having long heard of Mr. Zheng's reputation and sharing the same aspirations, gathered funds of 100,000 yuan in national currency and planned for two more years to complete the preparations. The company was named "Foci Grand Pharmaceutical Factory Co., Ltd." The company is about to open, and it is said that it will focus on (1) scientific research on Chinese medicines and (2) scientific manufacturing of Chinese medicines.

Social News

The Life of Working Women in New York (9)

— Lin

Clara Shi ate her lunch with great relish. She never lightly dismissed the joy of occupying a part of New York. She was a true city girl, pretending to possess it all, but her inclinations leaned towards music, crowds, frivolity, and laughter.

She spent a full hour eating her meal, then leisurely smoked a cigarette. Originally, she didn't like smoking, but at a charity event in a hotel, she saw many young women with cigarettes in their mouths, almost none of them not smoking. Many of her cigarette-buying customers were women. She felt smoking was a fashionable thing. She didn't inhale the smoke.

After lunch, she had to go back to work. George was coming this afternoon. George was a salesman who came to this hotel every week. Because he liked Clara Shi, he often took her out to eat. He was a generous spender, but people always felt he was a bit odd. He talked endlessly about business, but rarely mentioned his own affairs, except once when he emotionally talked about his mother. Clara Shi imagined he must be married. Once, she asked him this, but he didn't answer. She realized it was better not to ask.

When the afternoon began, she was already watching for him. He was very different from many people who came to the hotel. He seemed very happy to be friends with her, but not overly intimate. Clara Shi sometimes complained that all men were the same. George told her that she only saw the worst aspects of them.

"These men are mostly peaceful and family-loving in their daily lives. But when they come to New York, they are like children on vacation from school, and they have to do something."

Finally, George came in through the large revolving door. He gave the luggage he carried to the waiter, and then went straight to where Clara Shi was standing. He looked truly happy to see her. He said they would have dinner at seven o'clock.

Clara Shi felt very happy for the rest of the day. She treated customers with joy, making them feel that she seemed to be very happy in her job. By six thirty, she had nothing to do. Now she felt she wanted to buy that black crepe dress. The price of the dress was $19.75, which was five dollars more expensive than the clothes she usually wore. But anyway, her curly hair was always so lovely. She had her hair permed once a week, at a cost of $1.50. She felt it was very worthwhile.

She and George met in the hallway of a nearby hotel, because it was not very appropriate to see him in the hotel where she worked.

"Your funny face," George said, "Where shall we go to eat?"

"Wherever you say," she replied. She knew that the phrase "funny face" was a bit of George's affection for her.

"How about going to the California Wanderer Restaurant?"

"Ah, George, that's great!" This place was a bit far from the city and was truly a superior place, with beautiful music, elegant scenery, and excellent food. It took a car ride from the city. Clara Shi thought it was very extravagant. Besides, there was nothing wrong with sitting in a car with George.

The two people talked about nothing but unimportant jokes in the car. Clara Shi was very good at arguing. After about half an hour, they arrived at their destination. A doorman hurried to the car. How happy Clara Shi was for this little attention. All day long, she saw others enjoy this kind of compliment in the hotel lobby. Now, she actually received it herself. She also hoped that they would pick her up wearing evening dresses. She had a dress with beaded trim at home, and a light-colored scarf. The color was too light for this weather, but she felt it would be lovely if she wore it.

They picked a table for two next to the dance floor. Clara Shi swayed gently in the middle of the music. She ordered many delicacies. Ah, she also knew how to pretend to be a noblewoman. She and George got up to dance, glanced at other tables, and saw if anyone noticed her. She felt very happy because someone was indeed noticing her. Her heart fluttered up and down, which was truly what life was all about.

At half past eleven, George suggested they should go home. Clara Shi turned her head and smiled, "Yes, it's not good to stay here too long."

In the car going back, Clara Shi curled up and leaned towards George, wanting to be protected by him. But he did not accommodate her.

"Good night, kid," were his parting words. When she got to her room, she took off her shoes and didn't know how to spend the rest of the night. She thought to herself, taking her home at this time, the night was not deep. Ah, God, men treat Clara Shi as if she were a joke, or only show a little friendship. Of course, she didn't want rude companions, but she wanted George to give her something other than dinner and dancing. She wanted to marry someone like George, but they didn't mention marriage to her. Oh, she was just a cigarette girl.

Because she felt unhappy, and because she didn't make herself comfortable, she took off her clothes and crawled into bed. She really hated going home so early when her companions hadn't returned yet. (To be continued)

Fierce Competition Between British and Japanese Yarn Industries

Unfolding in China, India, and Southeast Asia

According to the Dongbao Newspaper, the competition between the British and Japanese yarn industries has intensified in China, India, and Southeast Asia since the British Eastern Yarn Industry Inspection Group returned home and agreed on countermeasures. Recently, a certain British company has sold a large number of rayon fabrics in Rangoon. One of these companies has the support of the Imperial Bank of India and uses the position of a special colonial bank. At the same time, relying on the deep recession, it adopts long-term settlement methods, taking advantage of harsh trading conditions. British yarn industries are also depreciating prices, and shipping companies are reducing freight rates, seeking tax-free entry and exit to various parts of the Far East. On the other hand, Japanese textile companies are engaging in freight reduction movements in order to compete, or secretly planning to establish a British-Japanese-Indian trade alliance, etc., to cope with the situation. In particular, Zhong, Japan, Toyo, and Fuji Yarn Factories are dedicated to correcting the defects in the market transactions they have already obtained, reorganizing finances, and further expanding the market. They have set up trading markets in major commercial ports such as China, Annam, the Straits Settlements, India, and Myanmar, and signed consignment contracts with merchants to facilitate transactions. In the future, the competition between British and Japanese yarn industries will become more intense.

Social News Submission Guidelines

(1) Text: limited to news about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, and rural areas.

(2) Health, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life. Pictures are limited to various lyrical paintings related to social life.

(3) Photographs: those about seasons, landscapes, animals, plants, people, and news photography are acceptable. Those with beautiful women in seasonal landscape photography are especially welcome.

Book Review

Uncle Liu San

— Li Chunsen

—School Play Collection, Volume 1—

Compiled by Gu Zhongyi

The school drama movement has indeed made progress this year. Almost all universities and middle schools have school drama groups. In the first half of the past 20th year, the entire life of the drama movement was simply supported by small-scale performances by school drama groups. It seemed that, except for a few young students who dedicated themselves to cultivating the field of dramatic arts, most people were disheartened. The misfortune of this kind of unhealthy drama movement itself must be injected with the new sap of youth. The author of Uncle Liu San also said in the preface,

The Chinese drama movement in recent stormy times is elusive, sometimes sinking and sometimes appearing. The future is vast, and it cannot but make those who work hard feel discouraged, passive, wait-and-see, and transformed. The efforts of many people, the management of decades, still see society highly praising the old dramas performed by Mei Lanfang, Ma Lianliang, and others. The future of new dramas is, as usual, "not optimistic." The momentum of new dramas is still "ill-fated."

From this point of view, he himself has certainly been rebuffed. The only thing he hasn't despaired of is his interest in the school drama movement. Let's see what the author says,

However, it cannot be said that there are no achievements at all. The rise of school drama is an undeniable fact. It is the only achievement of the drama movement in the past few decades. These achievements are cultivated among students who are full of vigor, good at responding to changes, and also reflect the final success of the Chinese drama movement in the future. The barren and barren Chinese society, in its current situation, is afraid that it has no hope of cultivating bright and splendid flowers of art. The school's garden, although small, is abundant and fertile, and has great potential for development. Therefore, our promotion of the school drama movement is indirectly promoting the entire new drama movement. Before we can immediately make achievements in society, let's first lay a foundation in the school. We don't need to be disappointed, discouraged, or at a loss. Let's all come to school to cultivate!

Indeed, young students accept the dramatic arts the earliest, and their future achievements must rely on them.

Mr. Gu has worked hard and the publication of the first collection of school plays is not a sign of the development of the school drama movement's future.

This collection contains a total of five short plays. Except for "Uncle Liu San," which is an original work, "Everyone Wins," "Seven Bodhisattvas," "Outsider," and "I Love the Dawn" are all translated and adapted. According to the editor in the preface, the compilation method of each collection is,

"In terms of materials, we strive to be diverse and broad, so that they can be adapted to various special schools, groups, and roles. In terms of writing style, we strive to be simple, easy to speak, and easy to understand. In terms of compilation, we originally planned to translate half and create half, but the editor was limited by the lack of time for creation and could not but take more existing foreign materials and adapt and supplement them to become concrete Chinese dramas. Sometimes the original work is too good, and the editor is unwilling to reluctantly translate it, so it is translated directly word by word to preserve its original style and charm as a rule."

Uncle Liu San depicts a character who values friendship. The opening scene first shows the epitome of a naughty child, which is Liu San's son, Guangzu, pacing boredly in front of the door. Coincidentally, his father's friend Zheng Ermazi escaped because he killed a bastard company commander in the camp. At this moment, there were chasing soldiers behind him, but Zheng Mazi had already been shot, and he was hungry and exhausted. He said that he could be saved if he went to Liu San's house. Who knew that because he had said something about Guangzu in front of Lao Liu, Guangzu made fun of him. He was just cunning and refused to hide him. Even when he was told about righteousness, he couldn't be moved. In the end, he was given two silver dollars as a benefit to tidy things up. After a while, the chasing soldiers came and asked him about Zheng Ermazi's whereabouts, but Guangzu still answered jokingly. Even when threatened, he was still calm, as if nothing had happened. Later, the platoon leader used the method of profit to lure him, sending him a silver watch as a price, and the result was success. But just when Zheng Ermazi was tied up, Liu San and his wife came back. He knew the details of the matter, and his face was already full of shame. When Zheng Ermazi scolded "A man is not worth dying, just don't be a traitor who sells friends," his inner conflict reached its extreme. After they left, he began to beat Guangzu, no matter how he begged for mercy, he finally died under Liu San's gun.

Speaking of Liu San's character, he is completely a Jianghu hero. Look at what he said,

"My grandfather, Liu Taigong, was a provincial governor and saved a few friends in the Jianghu who fell into the grass and became bandits. My father was willing to be cut in the waist for the sake of his brothers' righteousness. As for me, who doesn't know my name, Uncle Liu San, because I always put my friends in front and my personal feelings behind. Okay, okay, you have lost all of Uncle Liu San's face. You are the first traitor in my Liu family who is ungrateful. Living is also a disgrace to the ancestors." (Page 21) "Everyone Wins" is a play about a couple quarreling. The characters here are two couples, Ge Daocun and Wu Songzhen, Tao Sifan and Tang Yunhe. Yunhe felt that when she loved her husband very much, she was very serious about everything she asked for. Later, when she learned that her husband was not a god and had things he couldn't do, she kept quarreling with him. Later, in order to avoid quarreling, she used means to do everything he wanted, but love had flown out of the window. This time, Songzhen and her husband were playing at Yunhe's house, but they quarreled with her husband until she cried. Yunhe took this treasure to teach Songzhen, and Songzhen did what Yunhe said, but she was not happy, and she completely said it. When Daocun went to tell Sifan, he wanted to force her to quarrel with him, because this way he could get true love. Who knew that the motive for the quarrel could not be aroused, and he had no way but to threaten her with an affair. In the end, she failed, and so for a small matter, she quarreled again seriously. At this point, the curtain fell.

This seems to be a technique for controlling a wife, but in reality, love is really difficult to handle. Generally, people think that love after marriage is very difficult to maintain. This is the main theme of this play. This is based on Ida Lubleshi Ehjlich's Winners All and adapted.

"Seven Bodhisattvas" is a three-act play, written about seven beggars who dressed up as seven Bodhisattvas. Because they had no business, they saw the seven Bodhisattvas carved on the green rocks of Mama Mountain, and they were greatly worshiped by passers-by, so they came to use them. They stole three green embroidered robes, dressed up, and first went to the market to promote, saying that there was a prophecy in an old classic that the seven Bodhisattvas on Mama Mountain were going to be dressed up and enter the city. As a result, they succeeded. The citizens worshiped to the extreme. Everything they had never eaten before, they were now eating. But in the end, they could not dispel the citizens' doubts. The citizens sent people to Mama Mountain to investigate, but just when they couldn't even dream of it, the real Bodhisattvas came from the mountain and enlightened the seven beggars. When the citizens realized that their bodies were already cold, they thought it was because of their suspicion that the Bodhisattvas had turned into stones. This shows the foolishness of the world's worship. The original author of this play is Lord Dunsany's Gods of the Mountain.

"Outsider" depicts a husband, Bao Baye, who is very irritable and puzzled because his wife has an affair. In the middle, the comicality of the great doctor is inserted. The characters here are all incomplete. Bao Baye's soliloquy at the opening is the summary of the whole play.

"I am the most unfortunate man in the world. I have a wife who really bothers me to death. Not only can she not take care of the housework and make the home clean, clear, comfortable, and make me happy, but she also makes me lose my temper twenty times a day. She is not at home for a few days, running around everywhere, eating big meals, taking cars, and associating with those unscrupulous friends. Alas, poor Bao Baye, what a poor husband you are. But I have to clean her up. If I kill her, ... that won't work, then my life will not be guaranteed in the future. If I put him in jail, ... that won't work either, this slut will find a way to escape ... It's really terrible, what should I do ... " (Page 109)

This play is based on Moliere's The Salonwyof he Barbouille and participates in Chinese materials.

"I Love the Dawn" writes about how young men and women regard love as a toy. They were originally a close couple, but unexpectedly a rift occurred due to the accidental encounter with a poet and a woman. The girl fell in love with the poet at first sight, and the boy was equally enthusiastic about the woman. From then on, they thought that they should go their separate ways. They all felt a new excitement, which was more meaningful than the former. But they changed again in less than a week. They saw through the poet's and woman's pranks, and then they made up. A cobbler is inserted here, and he is present in every scene, and there is such a song in every scene,

"Love and I are very good,"

Until one day (fate) is exhausted, ——

Beautiful, brave and free, ——

I love and I are terrible,"

His words and actions are all lovely. He seems like a good teacher. Modern young people are all asking for love. They fantasize about a happy dream, but when they get love, they will feel dissatisfied. The result is that they make up trivial branches. This common morbid state is strongly implied in this play. This play is based on Adelaide C. Rowol's short play.

In summary, these four translated short plays have certainly achieved considerable success, but it cannot be said that they are completely flawless. It is precisely because these plays do not have much characteristic features, the plot is very simple, and there are also places that are worth discussing in terms of thought and skill. As for the various advantages, there are certainly many. However, I don't want to talk about it at this moment.

The content of the script has been roughly said, so if we take this book to dedicate to the drama groups of various schools, I personally still think that it is not very satisfactory. As mentioned above, our script is to adapt to the special environment of young students. Among the five short plays in this collection, except for "Uncle Liu San" and "I Love the Dawn," which still have some merits, the three plays "Everyone Wins," "Seven Bodhisattvas," and "Outsider," if they are performed on stage, I believe that there will be a strong sense of hesitation, but in the school drama aspect, it does not seem to be very necessary. I hope that in the next nine collections, we can make more contemporary school drama scripts. This is what we are looking forward to.

Finally, let's borrow the words of the author's preface to end this article,

"The drama movement is a career that can only be run by the cooperation of many people, and the most popular school drama movement that is being created needs the support of a group of loyal supporters ... Let's all work hard, cultivate, irrigate, and support this small flower of art."

Shanghai Market

Market News

▲ Ling Sheng Oil Ink Company of Zhifu Road, Zhejiang Road, announces that, because our new factory has been completed, we are giving away commemorative gifts. Anyone in the printing industry who comes or sends a letter to ask for them will receive two kinds of practical and useful things for free, but each family is limited to one gift.

▲ Dahua Electric Company announces that our company is founded by tycoons in the electric industry and wealthy merchants. We specialize in manufacturing wireless radio commercial, military, land, and sea large and small transceivers, as well as various application materials. We have abundant capital and a large scale. The temporary office is located at No. 168 Sichuan Road. The wireless radios on the ships of major commercial shipping companies in the region, such as China Merchants, Ningshao, Sanbei, Zhengji, Antai, Datong, National Shipping, French Liu Zhengji, Longmao, Heng'an, Taifeng, and Jitong, are all produced by our company. We have hired engineers with specialized wireless radio knowledge and physics doctors from European and American universities to work in our company, carefully study, and strive for perfection. Therefore, our products are excellent and have a good reputation. We have gained the trust of important people in the National Government and the praise of various shipping companies. There are countless government radio stations ordering military wireless radios. In this urgent autumn of suppressing bandits, there is no time to delay. Therefore, our company is working day and night to rush to manufacture them and successively send them to the front line for installation, in order to eliminate the communist bandits and achieve the full success of the revolution. The manager is Mr. Cao Zhongyuan, who recently returned from studying wireless radio at English, French, German, and Belgian universities. The chief engineer and supervisor is Dr. Yan Renguang, a physics expert who has long enjoyed a great reputation at home and abroad. The director of the business department is Mr. Ding Lucheng, the former Chinese assistant manager of the German company Lihe Foreign Trade.

Medical News

▲The Shanghai Electro-Therapeutic Clinic proclaims that the rapid progress in the medical field in recent years is truly astonishing. The precision of drug therapy is already known worldwide, while physical therapy has emerged as a dark horse, achieving remarkable feats and showing a tendency to surpass drug therapy. Germany and Japan have made considerable advancements in the research and implementation of this therapy. However, it seems that the medical community in our country has remained silent on this matter, which is regrettable. Now, Dr. Chen Yanbing, a specialist in physical therapy who studied in Japan, recognizing the lack of this therapy in the country, has purchased a large number of sophisticated electrotherapy devices from abroad. He has established the Shanghai Electro-Therapeutic Clinic at 198 Old Baizi Road in this city, allowing patients from all walks of life in our country to benefit from the "sweet dew" of 20th-century physical therapy. The clinic has now opened and is offering free medical treatment for one month, it is said.

▲The renowned doctor Zhang Chenglu of Hankou possesses profound medical knowledge and is particularly skilled in pediatrics and obstetrics. Having practiced in Shanghai for over a decade, he has saved countless lives. In recent years, he has been practicing at No. 1 Dunren Lane, Marlang Road, in the French Concession. Those seeking treatment are constantly at his door, especially those coming from Zhabei. Dr. Zhang, concerned about the suffering of the poor and sick in traveling back and forth, has recently secured premises at No. 13 Hexing Lane, Xiangshan Road, Zhabei, to establish a branch clinic. The hours are set from 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM. At the main clinic in the French Concession, he will be available from 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM, after which he will be at the Zhabei branch clinic, it is said.

▲The traditional Chinese medicine practitioner Zhou Zhilin proclaims that since the beginning of summer, the erratic climate has made people susceptible to illness. Currently, many people in the city are suffering from fever, headache, diarrhea, and coughs. Many cases of these symptoms have been successfully treated by the traditional Chinese medicine practitioner Zhou Zhilin. Mr. Zhou now has a clinic at Beixing Lane, at the intersection of North Nicheng Bridge and Xinzha Road, offering consultations in the mornings during the summer. His book, "Practical and Effective Prescriptions for Internal and External Medicine," can be obtained by sending a letter with a four-cent stamp for postage, it is said.

▲The Corden Trading Company proclaims that "Mathesin," the world-renowned and effective cure for gonorrhea and syphilis, is the latest invention of the German medical saint Dr. Adina. The tablets are purely made by electrolysis, hence their great efficacy. Whether for new or old cases of gonorrhea, it is effective after six hours of administration. This medicine can quickly cure and permanently eradicate severe cases of chronic gonorrhea that have not responded to surgery or injections. This company is the sole agent for the Far East, and the medicine will arrive in Shanghai soon, it is said.
